                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Achiote paste, Barbecue recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#achiotepaste #garlic #vegetables #mexicanoregano #spices #spice #annattoseeds #achiote #pestleandmortar #pork #cinnamon \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Achiote paste or Recado rojo or is a popular blend of spices from Mexico used to season meat or vegetables\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 156\n|PortionCalories = 39\n|DatePublished=25th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Tofu marinading in achiote paste\n |Servings = Servings: 4 - Makes 1 cup of [[Achiote|achiote]] paste\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 10 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Tofu marinading in achiote paste.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Even tofu tastes good in this</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.2</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Great vegetarian dish</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''[[Achiote]] paste''' or '''Recado rojo''' or  is a popular blend of [[Spices|spices]] from Mexico used to season [[Meat|meat]] or [[Vegetables|vegetables]]. Originally a Mayan blend, it is now strongly associated with the [[Mexican Cuisine|Mexican cuisine]] of Yucatan.\n\nThe [[Spice|spice]] mixture usually includes [[Annatto|annatto]], [[Mexican oregano]], [[Cumin|cumin]], [[Clove|clove]], [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]], [[Black pepper|black pepper]], [[Allspice|allspice]], [[Garlic|garlic]], and [[Salt|salt]]. The [[Annatto seeds|annatto seeds]] dye the mixture red, and this gives the [[Meat|meat]] or [[Vegetables|vegetables]] it seasons a distinctive red hue.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| &#188; cup [[annatto seeds]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Coriander seeds|coriander seeds]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Mexican oregano]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Black peppercorns|black peppercorns]]\n| 2 whole [[Cloves|cloves]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 5 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled\n| &#189; cup [[Bitter orange|bitter orange]] [[Juice|juice]] or 1/3 cup [[White wine vinegar|white wine vinegar]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Using a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]] or a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]], grind the dry [[Spices|spices]]\n| Peel and crush the [[Garlic|garlic]], mix with the [[Salt|salt]], [[Ground|ground]] [[Spice|spice]] mix and [[Orange juice|orange juice]] and mix to a smooth paste.\n| Rub the mixture onto [[Chicken|chicken]], [[Pork|pork]] or [[Fish|fish]] and [[Marinate|marinate]] in a cool place for 4-6 hours then cook as you would normally.\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#achiotepaste #garlic #vegetables #mexicanoregano #spices #spice #annattoseeds #achiote #pestleandmortar #pork #cinnamon </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

Originally a Mayan blend, it is now strongly associated with the [[Mexican Cuisine]] of Yucatan.\n\nThe [[Spice|spice]] mixture usually includes [[Annatto|annatto]], [[Mexican oregano]], [[Cumin|cumin]], [[Clove|clove]], [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]], [[Black pepper|black pepper]], [[Allspice|allspice]], [[Garlic|garlic]], and [[Salt|salt]].                         "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Aldi's Fiesta Chilli Con Carne with Cubed Steak\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#pressurecooker #sweetcorn #kidneybeans #aldisfiestachilliconcarnewithcubedsteak #chilliconcarne #rice #chillipepperrecipes #garlicrecipes #steak #beefrecipes #sherry\n|hashtagrev=12032020\n|description=A super tasty chilli con carne using bought sauce in a jar spiced up a little so it suits my taste\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|DatePublished=17th May 2023\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  2 hours, 5 minutes\n|PrepTime =  5 minutes\n|CookTime =  2 hours\n|TotalCalories = 617\n|PortionCalories = 154\n|Image = [[Image:Aldi's Fiesta Chilli Con Carne with Cubed Steak recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Tastes authentic</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This is now my preferred way to make chilli!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jeremy]] </span></span>\n}}\nI wanted to jot down a reminder for myself because the [[Chili con carne|chili con carne]] I made was absolutely delicious and incredibly easy. It had an authentic flavour, and the [[Meat|meat]] turned out incredibly tender thanks to the extended cooking time achieved by using a [[Pressure cooker|pressure cooker]].\n\nThis is now a regular staple, together with [[How long to cook Oakhurst Aldi Peri Peri Chicken King Kebab|Aldi's Peri-Peri King Kebab]].  We now make this, eat half and freeze the remainder for another meal together. \n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 jar of Aldi's Fiesta [[Chilli con carne|chilli con carne]] (Hot)\n| 1 kg of [[Stewing steak|stewing steak]]; ours is from [[Russell's Butchers of Upwell, Norfolk]]\n| 1 400g can [[Kidney beans|kidney beans]]\n| 1 340g can [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]]\n| &#189; teaspoon very [[Hot chilli powder|hot chilli powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Taste Sensation fajita seasoning]] mix\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Drain the [[Kidney beans|kidney beans]] and rinse well\n| Drain and rinse the [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]]\n| Cut the [[Steak|steak]] into fairly small pieces as they tend to be on the large size\n| Pour the Fiesta [[Chilli con carne|chilli con carne]] [[Sauce|sauce]] into a large bowl that will fit into your [[Pressure cooker|pressure cooker]]\n| Rinse the jar with a little water or [[Sherry|sherry]] if you're feeling lush!\n| Add the remaining ingredients and mix well\n| Pressure cook on heigh for 2 hours (would be done in 1 hour, but 2 makes the meat super tender)\n| Allow to de-pressurise naturally\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Aldis Fiesta Chilli Con Carne with Cubed Steak ingredients.jpg|All of the ingredients\nImage:Aldis Fiesta Chilli Con Carne with Cubed Steak mixed and ready to cook.jpg|Mixed well and ready to pressure cook\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nWe had this over two days; firstly with [[Taco shells|taco shells]] and then I had mine with [[Curly fries|curly fries]] and Anne had her second lot with [[Rice|rice]].\n===Chef's notes===\nThis was a superb [[Chilli|chilli]] with just the right heat.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilean recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pressure cooker recipes]]\n[[Category:Pressure cooked]]\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#pressurecooker #sweetcorn #kidneybeans #aldisfiestachilliconcarnewithcubedsteak #chilliconcarne #rice #chillipepperrecipes #garlicrecipes #steak #beefrecipes #sherry</code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Anticuchos de corazon",
                "revisions": [

                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Anticuchos de corazon recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#heart #anticuchosdecorazon #garlic #cumin #marinade #beef #redpepper #greenpepper #unusualrecipes #marinated #capsicum \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Anticuchos are popular and inexpensive dishes that originated in Peru, and popular also in other Andean states consisting of small pieces of grilled\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 401\n|PortionCalories = 80\n|DatePublished=26th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = 5\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 10 hours, 30 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 hours, 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Anticuchos de corazon recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Super street food</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This was nice and hearty \ud83d\ude02 </span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nAnticuchos are popular and inexpensive dishes that originated in Peru, and popular also in other Andean states consisting of small pieces of [[Grilled|grilled]] skewered [[Meat|meat]].\n\nAnticuchos can be readily found on streetcarts and street food stalls (anticucheras). The [[Meat|meat]] may be [[Marinated|marinated]] in [[Vinegar|vinegar]] and [[Spices|spices]] (such as [[Cumin|cumin]], aji [[Pepper|pepper]] and [[Garlic|garlic]]), and while anticuchos can be made of any type of meat, the most popular are made of [[Beef|beef]] [[Heart|heart]] (anticuchos de corazon). Anticuchos often come with a [[Boiled|boiled]] [[Potato|potato]] on the end of the skewer.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 Beef [[heart]]\n| 2 cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]]\n| &frac14; of a cup ground spicy [[red chili]]\n| 2 cups of [[malt vinegar]]\n| 1 teaspoon of ground [[cumin]]\n| 1 teaspoon of achiote ([[annatto]])\n| 1 teaspoon of [[salt]] \n| 1 teaspoon of ground [[black pepper]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place all the above ingredients, other than the [[Heart|heart]], in a bowl and mix thoroughly.\n| Clean the [[Heart|heart]], removing all [[Fat|fat]]. Cut into bite size cubes. Place the heart pieces into the [[Marinade|marinade]] mixture and leave to [[Marinate|marinate]] for about 10 hours or overnight. The heart should be completely covered.\n| After [[Marinating|marinating]], insert [[Meat|meat]] on [[skewers]]. At this stage if desired , some additional ingredients such as [[Green pepper|green pepper]] or [[Red pepper|red pepper]] ([[Capsicum|capsicum]]) or [[Corn|corn]]-on-cob (cut to a similar size to the [[Heart|heart]], may be also inserted on the skewers.)  \n| The skewered [[Heart|heart]] should then be cooked on a [[Barbecue|barbecue]] [[Grill|grill]], turning frequently and brushing with the [[Marinade|marinade]] mix. When they are well done they should be served immediately.\n}}\n===Variations===\nIf [[Heart|heart]] is not to your taste, try a less-authentic version using a good cut of [[Beef|beef]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Offal recipes]]\n[[Category:Peruvian recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#heart #anticuchosdecorazon #garlic #cumin #marinade #beef #redpepper #greenpepper #unusualrecipes #marinated #capsicum </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Arroz con pollo",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Arroz con pollo, Chilean recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #rice #arrozconpollo #cilantro #peas #tomatoes #paprika #diced #saffron #oliveoil #onion \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Arroz con pollo (rice with chicken) is a traditional dish that's common throughout Latin America especially in Cuba, Panama, Peru, Puerto Rico, Costa\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4105\n|PortionCalories = 684\n|DatePublished=8th December 2013\n|Author=Carla Cancio-Bello, J.D., on behalf of Cuban Cuisine UK\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 50 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Arroz con pollo recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">So pretty</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">A lovely dish, thanks Carla.  Here's hoping everything is good with you.  Long time no hear???</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n}}\n\nArroz con pollo ([[Rice|rice]] with [[Chicken|chicken]]) is a traditional dish that's common throughout Latin America especially in Cuba, Panama, Peru, Puerto Rico, Costa Rica, and the Dominican Republic. There is a widespread belief among Hispanics in the US that it originated in Puerto Rico but there is no direct evidence for this. However, it resembles [[Paella|paella]], a [[Spanish]] dish, both in its ingredients and cooking technique, and may very well be a New World adaptation of it.\n\nCommon ingredients for arroz con pollo include [[Rice|rice]], [[Vegetables|vegetables]], [[Fresh herbs|fresh herbs]] and [[Chicken|chicken]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.5 kg whole [[Chicken|chicken]] cut into serving pieces - [[Jointing a chicken|see here for step by step details]]\n| [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] to taste\n| [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 4 [[Cloves|cloves]] of fresh, minced [[Garlic|garlic]]\n| 1 medium [[Onion|onion]], chopped\n| 8 oz [[Diced|diced]] [[Red bell pepper|red bell pepper]]\n| 1 can (15 ounce) [[Diced|diced]] [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| &#189; tablespoon sweet [[Paprika|paprika]]\n| &#189; oz chopped [[Cilantro|cilantro]]\n| 6 cups [[Chicken|chicken]] [[Bouillon|bouillon]]\n| a handful of [[Cilantro|cilantro]]\n| 8 [[Saffron|saffron]] threads or 1 teaspoon of food colouring for [[Yellow rice|yellow rice]]\n| 2 cups medium or long-rain [[Rice|rice]]\n| 8 oz canned [[Peas|peas]] (thoroughly drained)\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Season the [[Chicken|chicken]] with two pinches of [[Salt|salt]] and a pinch of [[Pepper|pepper]].\n| Pour enough [[Olive oil|olive oil]] into a large [[Skillet|skillet]] to just barely cover the bottom.\n| Saut\u00e9 [[Chicken|chicken]] in [[Oil|oil]] until [[Brown|brown]]. There are two ways to proceed from here: Either remove the chicken from the [[Skillet|skillet]] or keep it there.\n| Saut\u00e9 [[Garlic|garlic]] until [[Brown|brown]]. Be careful, garlic burns easily.\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]], [[Bell pepper|bell pepper]], [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Paprika|paprika]]. Saut\u00e9 until the [[Vegetables|vegetables]] are tender.\n| Transfer the ingredients to a large [[Stewing|stewing]] pot.\n| Add the [[Cilantro|cilantro]], bouillon and [[Saffron|saffron]] (or food colouring). Bring to a rolling [[Boil|boil]].\n| Add the [[Rice|rice]] and mix well. [[Simmer]] over medium heat until the rice is cooked and the liquid is absorbed. Add more [[Broth|broth]] or water if the liquid evaporates before the rice is cooked.\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] to the pot (if you removed it previously) and cover it with [[Rice|rice]]. Wait two to three minutes to allow the chicken to warm.\n| Sprinkle [[Peas|peas]] on top of the [[Rice|rice]]\n}}\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilean recipes]]\n[[Category:Jamaican recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Cuban recipes]]\n\n[[Category:Peruvian recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #rice #arrozconpollo #cilantro #peas #tomatoes #paprika #diced #saffron #oliveoil #onion </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

It's been cooking for four hours now and smells amazing. I..\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|DatePublished=10th December 2019\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  7 hours, 10 minutes\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime =  7 hours\n|TotalCalories = 1512\n|PortionCalories = 378\n|Image = [[Image:Beef Skirt Steak Fajitas recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Glorious!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This takes a while to cook but it's well worth the wait, the smell while it cooks is fantastic.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nAnother experiment with [[Taste Sensation Seasonings]]; this time [[Taste Sensation fajita seasoning]].  It's been cooking for four hours now and smells amazing.  I am becoming very impressed with their products!\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 350g [[beef skirt]] (or [[Stewing steak|stewing steak]])\n| 3 tablespoons [[Taste Sensation fajita seasoning]]\n| 1 whole [[Lime|lime]], un-squeezed and sliced into eighths\n| 1 [[Red onion|red onion]], chopped\n| 1 [[Green bell pepper|green bell pepper]], de-seeded and chopped\n| 250 ml [[White wine|white wine]]\n| 200 ml water\n| 1 can of [[Red kidney beans|red kidney beans]], drained and well rinsed\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| [[Marinade]] the [[beef skirt]] in the [[Wine|wine]] for a few hours if you have the time\n| Pop the [[Meat|meat]] in the [[Slow Cooker|slow cooker]] and pour the [[Wine|wine]] over the [[beef skirt|skirt]] and add the water\n| Cover with the remaining ingredients and cook on a high setting for about six hours\n| Check it does not dry out and that the [[Meat|meat]] is tender and starting to break up.\n| Add the [[Kidney beans|kidney beans]] for the final hour\n| Stir well and serve\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe in warmed [[Flour tortillas|flour tortillas]] with a [[Salad|salad]] and slices of [[Citrus fruit|citrus fruit]]\n===Variations===\nA whole [[leek]], finely chopped looks good as a replacement for the onion, if leeks are in season.\n\n===Chef's notes===\n[[Beef skirt]] is a fabulous, inexpensive cut for this dish.  It does need a lot of cooking, but once it begins to break up into 'strings' as you can see in the 'plated-up' picture you know it's tender and ready to eat.  At this point you can turn the heat down and just keep the meat warm until you're ready to serve.\n\nI added the [[kidney beans]] to bulk out the meal a little, and also as a way to soak up the gorgeous flavours.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Chilean recipes]]\n[[Category:Ecuadorian recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooker recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooked]]\n[[Category:Taste Sensation recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#beefskirt #kidneybeans #beefskirtsteakfajitas #wine #greenbellpepper #tastesensationrecipes #leek #redkidneybeans #lime #whitewine #salad </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Black bean burritos recipe Cooking with chillies\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#beans #sourcream #blackbeanburritos #salsa #burritos #bean #chillies #baking #emmenthalcheese #sweetcorn #cheese \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is a quick-to-make recipe that uses prepared ingredients, but still allows you to tailor it to your particular taste\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1823\n|PortionCalories = 303\n|DatePublished=8th December 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6 - Makes 6 [[Burrito|burritos]]\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 35 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Black bean burritos recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Better than El Paso!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Much nicer than the prepared versions</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nThis is a quick-to-make recipe that uses prepared ingredients, but still allows you to tailor it to your particular taste.  [[Emmenthal cheese]] is obviously not authentic, but I just love it, so [[Emmenthal]] it is.  Use any [[Cheese|cheese]] of your choice.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 pack of [[Flour|flour]] [[Tortillas|tortillas]]\n| 175 g can of [[Black beans|black beans]]\n| 165 g can of [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]] kernels\n| 350 g bottle of [[Tomato salsa|tomato salsa]]\n| 150 ml tub of [[Sour cream|sour cream]]\n| 200g [[Emmenthal cheese]], [[Grated|grated]]\n| 3 fresh or [[Pickled|pickled]] [[Red chillies|red chillies]] (or to taste)\n| [[Freshly ground black pepper]]\n| [[Olive oil]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the oven to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Tip the [[Salsa|salsa]] into a bowl\n| Chop the [[Chillies|chillies]] finely, remove the [[Seeds|seeds]] if you don't want it too hot.\n| Rinse and drain the [[Black beans|black beans]]\n| Place 2/3rds of the [[Beans|beans]] in a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a metal blade and blend to a chunky paste\n| Add the blended [[Beans|beans]] and the remaining whole [[Beans|beans]] to the bowl\n| Add the [[Salsa|salsa]] to the bowl, stir in the [[Chillies|chillies]] and mix well\n| Reserve about 4 tablespoons of the [[Bean|bean]]/[[Salsa|salsa]] mix to a saucer to top the [[Burritos|burritos]]\n| Rinse and drain the [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]] and add to the bowl of [[Beans|beans]] with 2/3rds of the [[Sour cream|sour cream]] and mix well.  Keep the rest of the [[Cream|cream]] to serve with the [[Burritos|burritos]]\n| Lightly [[Oil|oil]] a [[Baking|baking]] dish\n| Fill 6 [[Tortillas|tortillas]] with the [[Bean|bean]] mix from the bowl, roll them up and place in the [[Baking|baking]] dish, seam-side down\n| Spread the reserved [[Bean|bean]] mixture from the saucer over the [[Burritos|burritos]] and cover with [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheese|cheese]].\n| [[Bake]] for 20 minutes or until heated through.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot with the remaining [[Sour cream|sour cream]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Cuban recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#beans #sourcream #blackbeanburritos #salsa #burritos #bean #chillies #baking #emmenthalcheese #sweetcorn #cheese </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This vegetarian pesto is made with butternut squash, always available at this festive time\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 810\n|PortionCalories = 202\n|DatePublished=3rd January 2015\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour, 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  1 hour\n|Image = [[Image:Butternut squash pisto.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Vegalicious!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Top marks Julia - A lovely vegetarian meal which we really enjoyed making.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nPisto is the [[Spanish]] equivalent of [[Ratatouille|ratatouille]].  This [[Vegetarian|vegetarian]] [[Pesto|pesto]] is made with [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]], always available at this festive time of year.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1.2 kg [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]], peeled and chopped into 2cm pieces - about 800g once prepared\n| 1 teaspoon of [[Old India Taco Seasoning]]\n| 6 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| A good pinch of [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 3 medium [[Onions|onions]], peeled and chopped\n| 1 [[Red pepper|red pepper]], deseeded, halved and cut into rings\n| 2 [[Green Indian chillies|green indian chillies]], thinly sliced, deseeded if you wish\n| 1 large [[Sprig of rosemary|sprig of rosemary]], left whole\n| 4 freshly picked [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n| 3 [[Cloves of garlic|cloves of garlic]], peeled and thinly sliced\n| 1 teaspoon [[Mexican oregano]]\n| A pinch of [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| A pinch of freshly [[Grated|grated]] [[Nutmeg|nutmeg]]\n| 180ml [[Passata|passata]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Port|port]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]]\n}}\n''' to garnish'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 tablespoons [[Pine nuts|pine nuts]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Pop the [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]] chunks into a [[Sieve|sieve]] and dust with the [[Old India Taco Seasoning]], set to one side.\n| Add the [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]] to a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]] or even a [[Wok|wok]].\n| Add the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and gently saut\u00e9 the [[Onions|onions]] for 15 minutes.\n| Add the sliced [[Red pepper|red pepper]] and [[Fry|fry]] for 10 minutes.\n| Now to liven it up; add the sliced [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]], whole [[Sprig of rosemary|sprig of rosemary]] and finally the [[Garlic|garlic]] slices.  [[Stir-fry]] these for a few minutes.\n| Give the [[Sieve|sieve]] of [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]] a shake to remove any liquid that may have leached out and add the [[Squash|squash]] to the pan.\n| Very gently saut\u00e9 the [[Squash|squash]] for 20 minutes, turning regularly.\n| After 20 minutes add the [[Passata|passata]], [[Port|port]], [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]], [[Mexican oregano]], and a grate of [[Nutmeg|nutmeg]] and heat for the final 10 minutes.\n| Remove the stem of the [[rosemary]] sprig and serve.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe garnished with [[Toasted|toasted]] [[Pine nuts|pine nuts]]\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you don't have [[Old India Taco Seasoning]], a pinch of [[Salt|salt]] and &#189; teaspoon of unsmoked [[Paprika]] will work just as well.\n{{Template:Pisto recipes}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Squash recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#butternutsquash #squash #pinenuts #cuminseeds #bayleaves #sieve #port #onions #nutmeg #butternutsquashpisto #oliveoil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Also, it is known to have been made without the [[Anchovies|anchovies]].  These were added much later to give the [[Sauce|sauce]] more body. \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Thermomix recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#thermomix #sauce #garlic #lemonjuice #mustard #mayonnaise #oliveoil #egg #parmesancheese #worcestershiresauce #grated </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

It is based on Jamie Oliver's recipe of the same name, though I recall having to adjust the quantities quite a bit from his original recipe.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 60 g [[Butter|butter]]\n| 2 large [[Onions|onions]], peeled and thinly sliced\n| 1 350g can of [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]] kernels, drained\n| 4 large [[Eggs|eggs]], beaten\n| 325 g coarse [[Yellow cornmeal|yellow cornmeal]]\n| 250 ml full [[Fat|fat]] [[Milk|milk]]\n| 1 heaped teaspoon [[Baking powder|baking powder]]\n| 6 tablespoons [[Plain flour|plain flour]]\n| [[Sea Salt|Sea salt]] & [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 150 g strong [[Cheddar cheese|cheddar cheese]], [[Grated|grated]]\n| 3 fresh [[Green chillies|green chillies]], 2 deseeded and chopped finely, the other cut into thin rings\n| [[Olive oil]] for greasing\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Butter|butter]] to a [[Frying pan|frying pan]] or [[Wok|wok]], give it a good grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]] and gently [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] for 15 minutes\n| Once the [[Onions|onions]] are golden, carefully add the drained [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]]\n| [[Stir-fry]] the [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]] for a few minutes then remove the pan from the heat and set to one side.\n| Add the [[Eggs|eggs]], [[milk]], [[Cornmeal|cornmeal]], [[Flour|flour]], [[Baking powder|baking powder]], a pinch of [[Salt|salt]] and most of the [[Cheese|cheese]] (leaving a little to sprinkle on the top) and beat until really well mixed.\n| Stir in the onions and sweetcorn and mix again.  It helps to leave the mixure to rest for 10 minutes after the first mix to allow the cornmeal to soak up the milk.\n| Grease two 22cm round flan sandwich tins with a little [[Olive oil|olive oil]], line the base with [[Greaseproof paper|greaseproof paper]] and pour in the [[Cornbread|cornbread]] mixture.\n| [[Bake]] for 20 minutes then carefully remove from the oven and sprinkle the top with the remaining sliced [[Chilies|chilies]] and [[Cheese|cheese]].\n| [[Bake]] for a further 10 minutes.\n| Remove from the [[baking tray]] and allow to cool on a wire rack for 15 minutes before serving.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Cheese and chilli cornbread ready to bake.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Cheese and chilli cornbread, ready to bake\nImage:Cheese and chilli cornbread ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|The ingredients for cheese and chilli cornbread\n</gallery>\n\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot or cold\n===Chef's note===\nDon't forget the [[greaseproof paper]] or you will find it very hard to get the cornbread out of the tins. :-(\n==See also==\nThis recipe is based on a version of Jamie Olivers 'Chilli cheese cornbread' from ''Jamie's America'' ISBN 978-0718154769\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cheeseandchillicornbread #sweetcorn #onions #cheese #bakingpowder #bake #greaseproofpaper #eggs #cornbread #butter #oliveoil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

 [[Cheese pupusas|pupusas]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 [[flour]] [[tortillas]]\n| 115g (4 oz)  thinly sliced cooked [[ham]]\n| 115g (4 oz)  [[grated]] [[Emmental]] or [[Gruyere cheese]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[double cream]]\n| 1 tablespoon chopped [[gherkins]] or [[capers]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix the [[grated]] [[cheese]] and [[double cream]]\n| Roughly chop the [[ham]] and stir into the [[cheese]] mixture\n| Heat 1 [[tortilla]] in a large heavy based [[frying]] pan\n| Place a quarter of the mixture in the centre of the tortilla\n| Cook for a minute or two\n| Fold [[tortilla]] in half, flip it over and cook for another minute\n| Keep warm while you cook the remaining quesadillas\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a [[salad]] or [[curtido]]\n===Variations===\nAdd some chopped pickled [[Jalape\u00f1o chillies]] if you like it spicy\n===Chef's notes===\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Quesadillas]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes|Quesadillas]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Quesadillas]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Quesadillas]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Quesadillas]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes|Quesadillas]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Quesadillas]]\n[[Category:Starters|Quesadillas]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Quesadillas]]\n[[Category:North American recipes|Quesadillas]]\n[[Category:Student recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tortilla #cheese #cheeseandhamquesadillas #doublecream #ham #grated #cornflour #flour #capers #panfried #gherkins </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

If you can obtain tomatillos, then do use them instead of tomatoes\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2427\n|PortionCalories = 606\n|DatePublished=17th December 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Served with yellow rice, peas and sweetcornc\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 55 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 35 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Chicken with pumpkin seeds and peanut butter sauce recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice \ud83d\ude0d</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I made this with tahini instead and it was great.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nA nice [[Tex-Mex]] twist on a simple [[Chicken|chicken]] [[Stew|stew]]. stock|chicken stock]]\n| 50g [[Home smoked bacon|Home smoked bacon]], [[Lardons|lardons]], streaky [[Bacon|bacon]] etc. [chopped]\n| 3 [[Cloves|cloves]] of [[Garlic]], peeled\n| 1 medium [[onion]], quartered\n| 1 teaspoon of [[cumin seeds]], crushed\n| 1 teaspoon of [[turmeric powder]]\n| 1 large stick of [[cinnamon]]\n| [[Olive oil]] for [[Frying|frying]]\n| 150 g [[Peanut butter|peanut butter]] (2 huge tablespoons)\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n''' to serve'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 4 [[Spring onions|spring onions]], seeds|pumpkin seeds]] until they start to pop, turn them often\n| Add them to a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a metal blade and grind them finely\n| Add the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], quartered [[Onion|onion]], peeled [[garlic]], [[chillies]], [[cumin seeds]] and [[turmeric powder]] and blend to a paste\n| Finally add the [[peanut butter]] and the [[chicken stock]]\n| Meanwhile, heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a frying pan, add the [[lardons]] and the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] until the chicken is golden [[Brown|brown]]\n| Add the blended sauce to a large pan, together with the cooked chicken pieces, stir, cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 35 minutes\n| Taste and season with [[Black pepper|black pepper]] and salt. \n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px [[Parsley|parsley]]\n===Variations===\nTry this with [[Pork tenderloin|pork tenderloin]] fillets instead of [[Chicken|chicken]]. Cut them into thin medallions and smash them flat before cooking.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Squash recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #tomatoes #cuminseeds #chickenstock #onion #chickenwithpumpkinsseedsandpeanutbutter #turmericpowder #peanutbutter #garlic #parsley #lardons </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Chilaquiles",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chilaquiles a cheese recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chilaquiles #chihuahuacheese #tortilla #chillipeppers #sourcream #sauce #onion #corntortillas #montereyjackcheese #tomatoes #garlic \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Chilaquiles are a traditional Mexican dish. Typically, corn tortillas cut in quarters and lightly fried are the base of the dish\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3897\n|PortionCalories = 974\n|DatePublished=8th August 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Chilaquiles - This looks weird, but it was really good! - My apologies to Catalina  and Ale!\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 25 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Chilaquiles recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Better than it looks here</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Delicious and unusual.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]])</span></span>\n}}\n[[Chilaquiles]] are a traditional [[Mexican]] dish. Typically, [[Corn tortillas|corn tortillas]] cut in quarters and lightly [[Fried|fried]] are the base of the dish. Green or red [[Salsa|salsa]] or [[Mole|mole]], is poured over the crisp [[Tortilla|tortilla]] triangles, called totopos. The mixture is [[Simmered|simmered]] until the tortilla starts softening. [[Eggs]] (scrambled or fried) and [[pulled chicken]] are sometimes added to the mix. The dish is topped with [[Cheese|cheese]] (typically grilled chihuahua  cheese ) and/or [[Sour cream|sour cream]] (crema), and it is served with [[Refried beans|refried beans]]. Like many dishes, regional and familiar variation are quite common.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 10 [[Corn tortillas|corn tortillas]] cut up in triangles ([[Tortilla chips|tortilla chips]])\n| &frac12; Cup of [[corn oil]]\n| 3 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]]\n| &frac12; [[Onion]]\n| 4 Medium Size [[Tomatoes]]\n| 3 [[Chilli peppers|chilli peppers]] (I suggest [[Serrano|Chile Serrano]])\n|* ''Serrano is classed as a hot chilli if you are looking for an equivalent''\n| 1 Cup of [[Sour cream|sour cream]] \n| 1 Cup of grated [[chihuahua cheese]] or [[Monterey Jack cheese]]\n| 1/2 a teaspoon of salt.\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| On a [[Deep frying|deep frying]] saucepan [[Fry|fry]] the [[Tortillas|tortillas]]\n| On a pot toast the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Chilli peppers|chilli peppers]],  [[Onion|onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]]. Liquidate the tomatoes, salt, [[Chilli peppers|chilli peppers]], onion and garlic.\n| As the [[Tortilla|tortilla]] is [[Frying|frying]] add the [[Sauce|sauce]].\n| Let the [[Tortilla|tortilla]] dunk into the [[Sauce|sauce]] but make sure the [[Chips|chips]] don't get too soft.\n| Add the [[chihuahua  cheese]] and it will melt with the heat.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Sour cream|sour cream]] and grilled [[chihuahua cheese]] on top.\n===Chef's notes===\nYou may add [[Epazote leaves|epazote leaves]], to the [[Sauce|sauce]]!\n===recipe source===\n* ''By [[User:User:CatyGPadilla|Catalina Garcia]] and Ale Angeles from Mexico''\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you're making this in Europe, a mild [[white cheddar]] is a good substitute for [[chihuahua cheese]] or [[Monterey Jack cheese]].\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you want to do this en Ecuador, use ripe mozzarella cheese and you can use paico is the same that epazote (A.V)\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chilaquiles #chihuahuacheese #tortilla #chillipeppers #sourcream #sauce #onion #corntortillas #montereyjackcheese #tomatoes #garlic </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }

to 1 teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] or to taste\n| 1 x 400g (14 oz) can of [[Plum tomatoes|plum tomatoes]], chopped\n| 142 ml (&frac14; pint) [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n| 1 teaspoon whole [[Grain|grain]] [[Mustard|mustard]]\n| 15 ml (1 tablespoons) [[Black treacle|black treacle]] or dark [[Molasses|molasses]]\n| 1 x 425 g (15 oz) can [[Red kidney beans|red kidney beans]], rinsed and drained\n| 1 x 425 g (15 oz) can black eye [[Beans|beans]], rinsed and drained\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 1 tablespoon chopped [[Parsley|parsley]]\n}}\n'''to garnish'''\n* 1 small [[Red pepper|red pepper]] or a few spring onions, chopped (optional)\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a pan, give it a good grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]] and then saut\u00e9 the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] until it softens and starts to take some colour, about 5 minutes.\n| Sprinkle the [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] over the [[Onions|onions]] and mix well.\n| Add the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Stock|stock]], [[Molasses|molasses]], [[mustard]] and the [[Beans|beans]].  Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] vigorously, uncovered for 15 minutes stirring now and then.  Simmer for longer if you want a thicker consistency.\n| Add the chopped [[Parsley|parsley]] , taste and adjust the seasoning if necessary.  [[Simmer]] for a further 5 minutes.\n| [[Roasted red pepper|Roast the red pepper]], remove the seeds and pith and  chop into slices\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Chilli beans reducing.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Chilli beans reducing\nImage:Chilli beans the ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Chilli beans, the ingredients\n</gallery>\n\n===Serving suggestions===\nGarnish with chopped [[Red pepper|red pepper]], or [[Spring onions|spring onions]] and serve with [[Bread|bread]] or [[Boiled rice|boiled rice]].  The cold rice in moulds was an especially good contrast with this dish.\n===Variations===\nUse any variety of [[Beans|beans]] or [[Pulses|pulses]].  [[Chick peas]] are nice with this.\n==See also==\n* [[Boston baked beans]]\n* http://www.channel4.com/4food/recipes/tv-show-recipes/the-fabulous-baker-brothers-recipes/baker-brother-beans-recipe\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chillibeans #beans #bread #chillipowder #redpepper #parsley #molasses #mustard #onion #maincourse #plumtomatoes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Chilli con carne (PC)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chilli con carne a beef recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#diced #tomatoes #chilli #staranise #kidneybeans #beans #redwine #simmer #pressurecooker #butter #oliveoil \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This recipe requires partial use of a pressure cooker\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2422\n|PortionCalories = 605\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 3\n|TotalTime = 1 day, 4 hours, 20 minutes\n|PrepTime = 1 day, 20 minutes\n|CookTime = 4 hours\n|Image = [[Image:Chilli con carne (PC) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Super tender</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">The trick is using the pressure cooker</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n\n}}{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\nThis recipe requires partial use of a [[Pressure cooker|pressure cooker]].  Ideally, this should be made a day or two before you want to eat it, so that the flavours can develop more.\n\n'''For the [[Kidney beans|kidney beans]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 50g [[Salt|salt]] dissolved in 500ml tap water\n| 150g [[Dried|dried]] [[Kidney beans|kidney beans]]\n| 500g [[Cherry tomatoes|cherry tomatoes]]\n}}\n'''For the [[Chilli|chilli]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| [[Olive oil]]\n| 450g [[Minced beef|minced beef]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and [[diced]]\n| 2 [[Star anise|star anise]]\n| 1 large [[Carrot|carrot]], peeled and [[Diced|diced]]\n| [[Garlic]] to taste, finely chopped\n| [[Green chillies]] to taste, chopped (remove [[Seeds|seeds]] if desired, but personally I don't bother)\n| 30g [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e\n| 375ml [[Red wine|red wine]]\n| 50g [[Heston's spiced butter]]\n| 3 medium [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Diced|diced]]\n| 500ml [[Beef Stock|beef stock]]\n}}\n'''To finish and serve'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 [[Red peppers|red peppers]], de-seeded, [[Roasted|roasted]] and peeled\n| Seasoning\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Put the [[Brine|brine]] ([[Salt|salt]] and water mixture) in the bowl with the [[Beans|beans]]. \n* Cover and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for 12 hours\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Put the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and 50g water into a [[Pressure cooker|pressure cooker]]\n| Put on the lid, bring to pressure over a high heat, reduce heat and cook for 20minutes\n| Remove from the heat and allow to cool before opening the lid\n| Put the pan on a high heat, stirring frequently until the liquid is reduced by half - about 10 minutes\n| Drain the [[Kidney beans|kidney beans]] and add to the pan.\n| Add enough water to cover the [[Beans|beans]] if necessary.\n| Replace the lid and bring up to pressure over a high heat.\n| Reduce and heat and cook for 20 minutes.\n| Leave the mixture until completely before opening.\n| Meanwhile, to start the [[Chilli|chilli]], coat the bottom of a large pan with [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and place over a high heat until [[Smoking|smoking]].\n| Add the [[Mince|mince]], in batches if necessary, so that it browns rather than [[Stews|stews]].\n| Remove and drain the [[Meat|meat]].\n| Add a little water to the pan to [[Deglaze|deglaze]] it, and tip the water and bits in with the drained [[Meat|meat]].\n| Reduce the heat to medium-high and thinly coat with another layer of [[Oil|oil]].\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]] and the [[Star anise|star anise]] and cook for 7-10 minutes until the onion begins to colour.\n| Add the [[Carrot|carrot]], [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Green chillies|green chillies]] and cook for another 10 minutes or until the carrot is soft.\n| Add the [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e, stir and cook for another 5 minutes until everything turns a brick-red colour.\n| Pour in the [[Red wine|red wine]] and allow to reduce by two thirds.\n| Remove the [[Star anise|star anise]] and discard.\n| Stir in the spiced [[Butter|butter]], the [[Mince|mince]], [[Diced|diced]] [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and [[Stock|stock]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] over a low heat for 2-3 hours, stirring occasionally.\n| To finish, fold the [[Beans|beans]] and chopped [[Peppers|peppers]] into the [[Chilli|chilli]] and bring to a [[Simmer|simmer]].\n| Season and stir in more spiced [[Butter|butter]] to increase the heat.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Rice|rice]], or [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheese|cheese]] and [[Sour cream|sour cream]] \n===Recipe source===\n* Lightly adapted from a recipe in Heston Blumenthal at Home ISBN 1408804409\n===Chef's notes===\nMy husband felt that it needed 5 chillies, rather than 2.  Also there was too much liquid, possibly caused by the fact that during simmering, it was covered for most of the time.\n===See also===\n* {{ChiliConCarne}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Pressure cooker recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#diced #tomatoes #chilli #staranise #kidneybeans #beans #redwine #simmer #pressurecooker #butter #oliveoil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chocolate chilli chicken Cooking with chillies recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #blender #chocolatechillichicken #sesameseeds #chocolate #mole #raisins #tortillas #molepoblano #sungold #breadcrumbs \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is my version of mole poblano chicken or chocolate chilli chicken. I prefer to use chicken legs because of the extra flavour you get when meat is\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2250\n|PortionCalories = 562\n|DatePublished=15th May 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 3\n|TotalTime = 1 hour\n|PrepTime = 25 minutes\n|CookTime = 35 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Mole poblano recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Sounds weird!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">However, it tastes really good.  Just don't use Cadbury's Dairy Milk for this!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n}}\n\nThis is my version of [[mole poblano]] chicken or [[chocolate]] [[chilli]] chicken.\n\nI prefer to use [[chicken]] legs because of the extra flavour you get when meat is cooked on the bone.\n\nI have been messing around with the ingredients for the [[mole]] so it's not totally authentic. Don't be afraid to experiment with the ingredients - the only thing I would not use is sweet [[milk]] chocolate!\n\nI did actually have [[tomatillos]] that I grew in a Grow-bag with my tomatoes. They were pretty meagre but it's nice to put them to a good use.  Remove the outer covering (husks) before use.\n\nThis was a total success.  Next time I would make double the sauce and freeze the other half as I think the [[mole]] would be good on steak too!\n\n\n'''For the [[boiled]] [[chicken]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 [[chicken]] legs, skin removed\n| 1 [[onion]], peeled and halved\n| [[Salt]] and [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n'''for the mole [[poblano]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 [[chipotle chillies]], (deseeded if you don't want it too hot)\n| 1 dried [[:Image:Chilesdearbol.jpg|Chile de \u00e1rbol]].\n}}\n(''Don't be afraid to experiment with whatever other chillies you can get hold of'')\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| &#189; a large onion, chopped\n| &#189; teaspoon [[black peppercorns]]\n| 2 [[clove]] buds\n| &frac14;  teaspoon dried [[oregano]] or [[marjoram]]\n| A very small piece of [[cinnamon stick]]\n| &#189; teaspoon of [[fennel seeds]]\n| &#189; teaspoon of [[cumin seeds]]\n| 1 teaspoon of [[coriander seeds]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[sesame seeds]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[ground almonds]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[raisins]]\n| 2 [[cloves garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| &frac14; cup [[breadcrumbs]]\n| 2 [[tortillas]], torn into small pieces\n| 5 tomatillos or [[tomatoes]] such as [[sungold]]\n| 25 g (1 oz) [[Green & Blacks Organic Chocolate]], unsweetened (I added a bit more at the end - taste and see first!)\n| 1.5 cups [[chicken stock]]\n}}\n\n'''To garnish'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 tablespoon [[sesame seeds]], lightly [[toasted]]\n| 1 [[orange]], quartered\n\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Simmering mole poblano.jpg|Mole poblano, simmering\nImage:Mole poblano ingredients.jpg|The mole ingredients\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n'''Mole poblano'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Don't be too fussy with the chopping as it's all going in the [[blender]] in the end.\n| Blitz all of the dry [[spices]] except for the sesame seeds to a powder in a [[coffee grinder]] or [[blender]] spice attachment\n| Add the remaining ingredients to the [[blender]] and blitz to a smooth sauce\n| Tip the dried spice mix into the sauce and give it a final blitz.\n| Pour the sauce into a pan, bring to a simmer and continue to simmer for 30 minutes stirring now and again\n}}\n\n'''Cooking the chicken legs'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the [[chicken]] legs in a pan with the onion halves and cover with boiling water, seasoning with salt and pepper\n| Return to the boil, then cover and simmer for 25 minutes\n}}\n\n'''Combining the two'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Remove the chicken legs and drain\n| Add the chicken to the mole (sauce) and heat for a further 10 minutes\n| Meanwhile, toast 1 tablespoon of sesame seeds in a small pan\n| Transfer the [[mole poblano]] and [[chicken]] to a serving dish and sprinkle with the toasted [[sesame seeds]]\n| Enjoy Mexico's national dish!\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with [[plain boiled rice]], [[guacamole]] and [[sour cream]] or [[creme fraiche]] and maybe a few [[tortillas]] and a [[green salad]].\n\n===Chef's note===\n\nI could not get Mexican [[chocolate]] so used Green & Blacks organic [[chocolate]], which is bitter and not too sweet. After all, the dish has [[raisins]] or [[sultanas]] which have a little [[sugar]] anyway.\n\n===Recipe too complicated?===\n\nIt's not really, but if you really can't be doing with all these ingredients, I have seen bottles of [[mole sauce]] in some of the larger supermarkets.  \n\nTry it out with the pre-made sauce, then come back and make the real thing!\n\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n* {{ChiliConCarne}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #blender #chocolatechillichicken #sesameseeds #chocolate #mole #raisins #tortillas #molepoblano #sungold #breadcrumbs </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Cochinita pibil",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Cochinita pibil, Garlic recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#cochinitapibil #marinade #chillies #roast #tequila #onion #foil #bayleaves #pork #julienned #roasting \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Cochinita pibil, puerco pibil or Mexican pit-pork is a traditional Mexican slow-roasted pork dish from the Yucatan. Preparation of traditional\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4404\n|PortionCalories = 734\n|DatePublished=28th July 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 day, 5 hours\n |PrepTime = 1 day, 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 4 hours 45 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Cochinita pibil recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Firepit Pork</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Mexican Perfection.  Lots of lime, lots of chili, lots of annatto!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Cochinita pibil''', '''puerco pibil''' or '''Mexican pit-pork''' is a traditional [[Mexican]] slow-roasted pork dish from the Yucat\u00e1n.\n\nPreparation of traditional cochinita or puerco pibil involves [[marinating]] the [[meat]] in strongly acidic [[citrus juice]], colouring it with [[annatto seed]], and [[roasting]] the [[meat]] while it is wrapped in banana leaf. [[Tin foil]] now provides a modern substitute.\nTraditionally, cochinita pibil was buried in a pit with a fire at the bottom to [[Roast|roast]] it. The Mayan word \"pibil\" means \"buried\".\n\n\n'''Grind to a powder'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2.5 tablespoons [[Annatto seeds|annatto seeds]] \n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] \n| 1.5 teaspoons [[Peppercorns|peppercorns]] \n| 1/2 a teaspoon of [[allspice powder]] or 8 [[Allspice berries|allspice berries]] \n| 5 whole [[Cloves|cloves]]\n| 1/2 a teaspoon of [[dried oregano]] \n}}\n'''[[Marinade]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and roughly chopped\n| 2 [[Scotch bonnet chili peppers]] (or [[Chillies|chillies]] of choice) \n| 80 ml [[Orange juice|orange juice]] \n| 80 ml [[Red wine vinegar|red wine vinegar]] \n| 1 tablespoon (30 ml) [[Salt|salt]] \n| 8 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled. \n| [[Juice|juice]] of 3 [[Lemons|lemons]] \n| splash of [[Tequila|tequila]]\n| 2 [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n| 1.3 kg [[Pork shoulder|pork shoulder]] \n}}\n'''Misc'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| Aluminium [[Foil|foil]]\n| 12 [[Taco shells]], or [[Tortillas|tortillas]] for serving\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Add the [[Spices|spices]] to a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] or [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]] and grind to a powder.\n* De-[[Seed|seed]] and roughly chop the [[Chillies|chillies]]\n* Add the [[Onion|onion]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Citrus|citrus]] juices, [[Vinegar|vinegar]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Spice|spice]] powder to a [[Blender|blender]] and liquidise.\n* Remove and discard the [[Pork rind|pork rind]] and cut the [[Pork|pork]] into 5cm (2\") cubes. Retain some of the [[Fat|fat]].\n* Place the [[Marinade|marinade]] ,[[bay leaves]] and the [[Pork|pork]] in a large [[lock and lock]] box or [[Tupperware]] container, shake well and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for 24 hours, mixing now and then.\n* For a little extra flavour, quarter the juiced [[lemons]] and add then to the marinade, discard before cooking.\n\n\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3) (see Chef's note)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Line a large [[Roasting|roasting]] tin with a large sheet of [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]].\n| Add the [[Meat|meat]] and [[Marinade|marinade]] and seal with the [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]]. [[Banana leaves]] can be used here, though it is still an idea to use tin-[[Foil|foil]] to provide a really good seal.\n| [[Roast]] for 4.5 hours.\n| Remove the [[Meat|meat]] and rest for 15 minutes.\n| Shred with a fork.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Cochinita pibil marinade.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Cochinita pibil marinating\nImage:Cochinita pibil ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|The ingredients for cochinita pibil\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nAs far as I can ascertain, the traditional way to serve this would be whole on [[plain rice]] with a salad and [[black beans]] or to shred the meat and serve in a rolled [[flour tortilla]] with a little [[salsa]].\n\nWhen we had this, somewhat unconventionally, we treated Cochinita pibil as you would [[Peking duck]].  Shred the pork, serve with [[julienned]] [[spring onions]], [[julienned]] [[cucumber]], [[green salad]], halved [[flour tortillas]], [[sour cream]], [[garlic mayonnaise]] and a variety of Chinese [[sauces]] such as [[plum sauce]], [[hoisin sauce]] etc.  Spread a [[tortilla]] with [[dips of your choice]], add a little salad and shredded pork, roll up and devour.  An absolute and total success!\n\nThe fourth time I cooked this, we ate half of it 'Chinese style' and made a wonderful curry with the second half. Just fried up some onions, celery, garlic with my favourite [[curry paste]], added a can of [[coconut milk]] and a can of [[chick-peas]] simmered it for an hour or so and served it with rice and peas. That stretched it out for another 2 days!    \n\n===Variations===\nI had no [[tequila]] so used [[dark rum]] instead.\nIn Mexico we use sour orange juice, not the regular oranges, but you can use only lemon juice and vinegar.\n\n===Chefs' note===\n2 unseeded [[Scotch bonnet chili peppers]] made this dish very hot, delicious,but bearable.  Remove the seeds if you don't want it too hot, or use a different [[chilli]].\n\nIf you have made the dish very (chili) hot, it's probably a good idea to separate the meat from the sauce before shredding the meat and serve the sauce separately.  For the sake of you heart, leave it to settle for a bit then drain most of the fat off.  It will be just as delicious, but much better for you.\n\nHaving made this a number of times, I now follow Jamie Oliver's idea for cooking [[slow roast lamb]], let the [[oven]] reach its highest setting, the moment you put the meat in the oven, reduce the heat to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3).\n====No chillies in authentic Mexican cochinita pibil====\nYou can avoid using chilli, in Mexico, Cochinita Pibil is not hot at all, we don't use any chilli. -- [[User:Myrna_Amor_Miranda]]\n{{Template:See-also-pulled-pork}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cochinitapibil #marinade #chillies #roast #tequila #onion #foil #bayleaves #pork #julienned #roasting </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

title": "Cochinita pibil (slow cooker recipe)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title= Cochinita pibil - A Mexican slow-cooker recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#pork #chillies #bayleaves #onion #tequila #marinade #cochinitapibil #lemons #garlic #julienned #lockandlock \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Cochinita pibil, puerco pibil (Mexican pit-pork) is a fantastic traditional Mexican slow-roasted pork dish from the Yucat\u00e1n. Ideal for use in a slow-cooker (crockpot)\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4379\n|PortionCalories = 729\n|DatePublished=13th July 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 day, 8 hours, 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 1 day, 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 8 hours\n |Image = [[Image:Cochinita pibil recipe slow cooked.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">May favourite meal</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.82</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Especially cooked so slowley</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Carla_Cancio-Bello,_J.D.,_on_behalf_of_Cuban_Cuisine_UK|Carla]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Cochinita pibil''', '''puerco pibil''' or '''Mexican pit-pork''' is a traditional [[Mexican]] slow-roasted pork dish from the Yucat\u00e1n.\n\nPreparation of traditional cochinita or puerco pibil involves [[marinating]] the [[meat]] in strongly acidic [[citrus juice]], colouring it with [[annatto seed]], and [[roasting]] the [[meat]] while it is wrapped in banana leaf. [[Tin foil]] now provides a modern substitute.\n\nTraditionally, cochinita pibil was buried in a pit with a fire at the bottom to [[Roast|roast]] it. The Mayan word \"pibil\" means \"buried\".\n\nThis version is identical to the [[Cochinita pibil|original recipe]] except that is cooked in a slow cooker. \n\n\n'''Grind to a powder'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2.5 tablespoons [[Annatto seeds|annatto seeds]] \n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]] \n| 1.5 teaspoons [[Peppercorns|peppercorns]] \n| 1/2 a teaspoon [[allspice powder]] or 8 [[Allspice berries|allspice berries]] \n| 5 whole [[Cloves|cloves]]\n| 1/2 a teaspoon [[dried oregano]] \n}}\n'''[[Marinade]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and roughly chopped\n| 2 [[Scotch bonnet chili peppers]] (or [[Chillies|chillies]] of choice) \n| 80 ml [[Orange juice|orange juice]] \n| 80 ml [[Red wine vinegar|red wine vinegar]] \n| 1 tablespoon (30 ml) [[Salt|salt]] \n| 8 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled. \n| [[Juice|juice]] and zest of 2 [[Lemons|lemons]] and one [[lime]] \n| splash of [[Tequila|tequila]]\n| 2 [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[jaggery]] or [[muscovado sugar]]\n| 1.3 kg mixture of [[Pork shoulder|pork shoulder]] and [[Pork]] cheek.\n}}\n'''Misc'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 12 [[Taco shells]], or [[Tortillas|tortillas]] for serving\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Add the [[Spices|spices]] to a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] or [[Mortar and pestle|mortar and pestle]] and grind to a powder.\n* De-[[Seed|seed]] and roughly chop the [[Chillies|chillies]]\n* Add the [[Onion|onion]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Citrus|citrus]] juices, [[Vinegar|vinegar]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Spice|spice]] powder to a [[Blender|blender]] and liquidise.\n* Remove and discard the [[Pork rind|pork rind]] and cut the [[Pork|pork]] into 5cm (2\") cubes. Retain some of the [[Fat|fat]].\n* Place the [[Marinade|marinade]] ,[[bay leaves]] and the [[Pork|pork]] in a large [[lock and lock]] box or [[Tupperware]] container, shake well and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for 24 hours, mixing now and then.\n* For a little extra flavour, quarter the juiced [[lemons]] and [[limes]] and add them to the marinade. Discard the lemons and limes before cooking.\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place in the [[slow cooker]] and cook for 8 hours on low.\n| Shred the meat with a fork and serve.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Cochinita pibil marinade.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Cochinita pibil marinating\nImage:Cochinita pibil ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|The ingredients for cochinita pibil\n</gallery>\n\n===Serving suggestions===\nAs far as I can ascertain, the traditional way to serve this would be whole on [[plain rice]] with a salad and [[black beans]] or to shred the meat and serve in a rolled [[flour tortilla]] with a little [[salsa]].\n\nWhen we had this, somewhat unconventionally, we treated Cochinita pibil as you would [[Peking duck]].  Shred the pork, serve with [[julienned]] [[spring onions]], [[julienned]] [[cucumber]], [[green salad]], halved [[flour tortillas]], [[sour cream]], [[garlic mayonnaise]] and a variety of Chinese [[sauces]] such as [[plum sauce]], [[hoisin sauce]] etc.  Spread a [[tortilla]] with [[dips of your choice]], add a little salad and shredded pork, roll up and devour.  An absolute and total success!\n\nThe fourth time I cooked this, we ate half of it 'Chinese style' and made a wonderful curry with the second half. Just fried up some onions, celery, garlic with my favourite [[curry paste]], added a can of [[coconut milk]] and a can of [[chick-peas]] simmered it for an hour or so and served it with rice and peas. That stretched it out for another 2 days!    \n\n===Variations===\nI had no [[tequila]] so used [[dark rum]] instead.\n\n===Chefs' note===\n2 unseeded [[Scotch bonnet chili peppers]] made this dish very hot, delicious,but bearable.  Remove the seeds if you don't want it too hot, or use a different [[chilli]].\n\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n\nIf you have made the dish very (chili) hot, it's probably a good idea to separate the meat from the sauce before shredding the meat and serve the sauce separately.  For the sake of your heart, leave it to settle for a bit then drain most of the fat off.  It will be just as delicious, but much better for you.\n\nHaving made this a number of times, I now follow Jamie Oliver's idea for cooking [[slow roast lamb]], let the oven reach its highest setting, the moment you put the meat in the oven, reduce the heat to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3).\n==See also==\n* [[Cochinita pibil]] (same recipe, oven cooked)\n* [[The renowned Mr Brown Pulled Pork - Oriental]]\n* [[Beer pickled belly of pork]]\n* [[Pulled pork]]\n* [[Slow roast recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:Slow cooker recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pork #chillies #bayleaves #onion #tequila #marinade #cochinitapibil #lemons #garlic #julienned #lockandlock </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Makes about 10 [[tortillas]]\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 1 hour 35 minutes\n|PrepTime = 1 hour 20 minutes\n|CookTime = 15 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Tortilla press2.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Delicious</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I love the special aroma of anything made with masa</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThese delicious [[corn tortillas]] are easy to make, though best made with a [[tortilla press]] if you can get hold of one.\n\nYou '''must''' use [[masa harina]] as [[cornmeal]] will not work.\n\n{{RecipeIngredientsTM\n| 250g [[masa harina]]\n| 330 ml hot water\n| 1/2 a teaspoon table [[salt]]\n}}\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place all of the ingredients into the bowl '''10 seconds / Speed 7''', then '''1 minute / Knead'''.\n| Rest for at least 1 hour then shape into 10 equal sized balls.\n| Using a [[tortilla press]] or [[rolling pin]], place a ball of dough between two non-stick sheets ([[Bake-O-Glide]] or similar) and press into shape\n| Heat a frying pan to a medium high temperature (but with no oil).\n| Cook each tortilla on one side for 15 seconds.\n| Turn and cook for 45 seconds.\n| Turn again and cook for a further 15 seconds.\n| They should have brown speckles.\n}}\n===Serving suggestion===\n\nCan be eaten as they are, fried, wrapped around [[beans]], [[salad]], [[chicken]], [[cheese]] etc.\n\nUse as suggested in your recipe\n*Make [[Cheese pupusas]] or [[Dobladas]] with your homemade [[maize tortillas]]\n===Variations===\n\nAdd 1-2 teaspoons [[chilli powder]] and/or 2-3 teaspoons [[garlic powder]] to the mixture.\n\n===Chef's note===\n\nIf you don't have a [[tortilla press]], use 2 chopping boards or just two sheets of wood as a substitute. title": "Corn tortilla recipe (V)",

The Panasonic SD 253 and similar models have a 45 minute pizza dough setting that is perfect for tortilla dough.\n| Rest for at least 1 hour then shape into 10 equal sized balls.\n| Using a [[tortilla press]] or [[rolling pin]], place a ball of dough between two non-stick sheets ([[Bake-O-Glide]] or similar) and press into shape\n| Heat a frying pan to a medium high temperature (but with no oil).\n| Cook each tortilla on one side for 15 seconds.\n| Turn and cook for 45 seconds.\n| Turn again and cook for a further 15 seconds.\n| They should have brown speckles.\n}}\n===Serving suggestion===\nCan be eaten as they are, fried, wrapped around [[beans]] etc.\n\nUse as suggested in your recipe\n===Variations===\nAdd 1-2 teaspoons [[chilli powder]] and/or 2-3 teaspoons [[garlic powder]] to the mixture.\n===Chef's note===\nIf you don't have a [[tortilla press]], use 2 chopping boards or just two sheets of wood as a substitute.  Place ball of [[dough]] between two non-stick surfaces such as small squares of [[Bake-O-Glide]] and stand on them!\n===Suppliers===\nSee the [[Tortilla Press]] page for UK suppliers.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Tortilla]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Tortilla]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Tortilla]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking|Tortilla]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes|Tortilla]]\n[[Category:Starters|Tortilla]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites|Tortilla]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Tortilla]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Tortilla]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes|Tortilla]][[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tortillapress #masaharina #dough #beans #chillipowder #tortillas #garlicpowder #rollingpin #cornmeal #corntortillas #breadmaker </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Crab quesadillas",
                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Crab quesadillas recipe Cooking with chillies\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#crabmeat #tortillas #onions #oliveoil #peppers #culinaryoilspray #mascarponecheese #chillipowder #sweetpepper #cheddarcheese #crabquesadillas \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A quesadilla is a dish in Mexican cuisine where cheese is placed on a cooking wheat or corn flour tortilla and then folded over and cooked until the\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2760\n|PortionCalories = 690\n|DatePublished=20th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Quartered quesadillas\n|Servings = 4 as a main, 6 to 8 as a [[starter]]\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 30 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 15 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Cheese and ham quesadillas recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">This is my Street Food</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Can't find this anywhere, so I have to make it myself - this works well for me.</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nA quesadilla is a dish in Mexican cuisine where [[cheese]] is placed on a cooking [[wheat]] or [[corn flour]] [[tortilla]] and then folded over and cooked until the cheese melts. These would go really well with our  [[Mango salsa]]\n\nQuesadillas are similar to the dish from San Salvador; [[Cheese pupusas|pupusas]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450 g (1 lb) fresh [[crabmeat]]\n| 1 packet of [[flour]] [[tortillas]] \n| 1 red [[sweet pepper]], cut into thin strips \n| 1 green [[sweet pepper]], cut into thin strips \n| &#189; a [[red onion]], peeled and thinly sliced\n| 1 tablespoon [[olive oil]] \n| 225 g (8 oz) [[mascarpone cheese]] \n| A good pinch of [[chilli powder]] \n| Good handful of [[coriander leaves]], finely chopped\n| 1 cup [[grated]] [[cheddar cheese]]\n| [[Culinary oil spray|Cooking oil spray]], I prefer [[olive oil]] for health reasons\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the oven to 230 \u00b0C (450 \u00b0F - Gas 8)\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[olive oil]] in a [[frying pan]]\n| Add the [[onions]] and [[peppers]] and [[fry]] until the [[onions]] are translucent \n| Meanwhile, into a large bowl, sift the [[crabmeat]] and remove any shell fragments\n| Stir the [[mascarpone cheese]] into the [[crabmeat]], add the [[coriander]] and [[chilli powder]] and mix well \n| Spray half of the [[tortillas]] with [[Culinary oil spray|cooking spray]]. Lay them [[oil]] side down on [[baking]] sheets \n| Add equal portions of the [[crabmeat]] and then [[onions]] and [[peppers]]\n| Sprinkle with the [[Cheddar cheese]]\n| Place the remaining [[tortillas]] on top and spray with cooking spray \n| [[Bake]] for about 10 minutes or until golden [[brown]]\n| Rest for 3 minutes then cut into quarters and serve\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot with [[Mango salsa]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#crabmeat #tortillas #onions #oliveoil #peppers #culinaryoilspray #mascarponecheese #chillipowder #sweetpepper #cheddarcheese #crabquesadillas </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
