                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Picante guacamole recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#guacamole #cup #avocados #picanteguacamole #limes #garlic #onions #recipesfromothersites #juice #serrano #hassavocados \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This guacamole recipe is courtesy of Mextrade.co.uk and originates from Picante Mexican Grill, Blackfriars\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 726\n|PortionCalories = 181\n|DatePublished=3rd June 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Picante guacamole recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">\ud83e\udd51\ud83e\udd51\ud83e\udd51</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Spicy dip!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis [[guacamole]] recipe is courtesy of [[Mextrade.co.uk]] and originates from the now extinct Picante Mexican Grill, Blackfriars, London\n\nProper [[Guacamole|guacamole]] is absolutely glorious, when made the traditional way with the right ingredients. Using [[Serrano]] [[Chilli pepper|chilli pepper]] adds a slightly nutty flavour that pairs very nicely with has [[Avocados|avocados]]. We have tried many brands over the years and exclusively use La Coste\u00f1a for their unbeatable flavour.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 2 [[Hass avocados]] (medium size)\n| &#8531; [[Cup|cup]] fresh [[Tomato|tomato]], chopped (about 1 medium)\n| &#8531; [[Cup|cup]] white [[Onion|onion]], finely chopped \n| 1 medium [[Clove|clove]] [[Garlic|garlic]], very finely chopped-ideally use a [[Garlic press|garlic press]]\n| &#8531; [[Cup|cup]] [[Coriander|coriander]], finely chopped (cut off steams just below 2nd leaves)\n| &#189; [[Lime|lime]], juiced\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 3 teaspoons La Coste\u00f1a Serrano escabeche (the [[Marinate|marinate]] liquid from the tin) \n| 2 [[Serrano chillies|serrano chillies]] finely chopped\n| Pinch [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Add all of the ingredients to a bowl\n| Using a fork, mix for a minutes to ensure everything is evenly distributed\n| Serve immediately\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nDo not use any other [[Avocados|avocados]] than Haas as they do not have the correct texture or flavour to make [[Guacamole|guacamole]], Haas are generally very dark in colour and have rough skin.\n\nOnly use perfectly ripe [[Avocados|avocados]], if the flesh is too firm or grey, it doesn't belong in [[Guacamole|guacamole]]. Grey avocados belong in the compost heap.\n\n[[Limes]] may yield variable amounts of [[Juice|juice]], so follow your taste buds. I personally prefer less [[Lime juice|lime juice]], but it is a key [[Ingredient|ingredient]], as it acts a natural [[Preservative|preservative]] and prevents the [[Avocado|avocado]] flesh from turning colour.\n\n''Jason Coolbaugh - Picante Grill''\n\n{{GuacamoleRecipes}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:MexTrade.co.uk recipes]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n===Recipe source===\n{{Template:RecipeCourtesyOfMexTrade.co.uk}}\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#guacamole #cup #avocados #picanteguacamole #limes #garlic #onions #recipesfromothersites #juice #serrano #hassavocados </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Pineapple vinegar",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Pineapple vinegar, Vegetarian recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#pineapple #pineapplevinegar #litres #vinegar #demerara #cheesecloth #dough #pickled #mexican #muscovado #jaggery \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Well this recipe failed miserably\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 52\n|PortionCalories = 52\n|DatePublished=12th April 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Pineapple vinegar - the beginning\n |Servings = 1\n |PrepTime = 504 hours\n |Difficulty = 3\n |TotalTime = 504 hours\n |CookTime = none\n |Image = [[Image:Pineapple vinegar - the beginning.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Inglorious failure :(</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">1</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">A waste of time and effort.  In the bin!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n==ABSOLUTE FAILURE==\n'''Well this recipe failed miserably.  No 'mother' appeared, and rather than clearing even after filtering, it grew cloudier and cloudier and smelt like badly fermenting beer.'''\n'''You are welcome to try this and see if you get better results than I did. In the meantime, I will do more research, try again, and document the results.  If you have better luck or any ideas, do please update the [[Talk:Pineapple_vinegar|comments page]].'''\n\n[[Mexican]] recipes often call for [[Pineapple|pineapple]] [[Vinegar|vinegar]], and now you can make your own with this simple recipe.  A little like sour [[Dough|dough]], once you have your ''mother or starter'', you can continue making more batches with just water and [[Sugar|sugar]].  The process can take up to 8 weeks or more, so don't expect instant results.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| The peelings from half of a fresh, washed, [[pineapple]]\n| Only the peelings are needed for this recipe, so use the good parts of the peeled and cored [[pineapple]] in [[:Special:Whatlinkshere/Pineapple|one of these recipes!]]\n| 4 heaped tablespoons raw [[Sugar|sugar]] ([[Demerara|demerara]], [[Muscovado|muscovado]], [[Jaggery|jaggery]] etc)\n| 1.5 [[Litres|litres]] water\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix the peelings, sugar and water together in a sterilised container and drape with a [[cheesecloth]]\n| Leave in a sunny warm place to ferment. In the UK, a warm conservatory is excellent for this\n| It should start fermenting after 3 days and become acidic\n| It will begin cloudy but should clear and gradually turn a dark amber - this may take 3 weeks or more\n| In a further 3 weeks, the ''mother or starter'' (a white disc of mould) should form - once this forms and is quite solid, the vinegar can be strained and bottled.\n| The ''mother/starter'' can be placed in more water and sugar without the need for more [[pineapple]] to create more vinegar.\n| It may be possible to freeze the ''mother'' for later use - watch this space to see if this worked for me!\n}}\n===Servings===\nServings: 140 - Makes about 1.4 [[Litres|litres]] of [[Pineapple|pineapple]] [[Vinegar|vinegar]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Cookery cheats]]\n[[Category:Dips and sauces]]\n[[Category:Pickles and preserves]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Pickled]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pineapple #pineapplevinegar #litres #vinegar #demerara #cheesecloth #dough #pickled #mexican #muscovado #jaggery </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Puerco en naranja",
                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Puerco en naranja, Meat recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#puercoennaranja #juice #fat #roast #oranges #roastingtray #orange #pork #peppercorns #brownsugar #dutchoven \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Another Mexican slow roast pork recipe that is quite similar to Cochinita pibil\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4246\n|PortionCalories = 1061\n|DatePublished=19th January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Puerco en naranja - delicious!\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 15 hours 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 12 hours 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 3 hours\n |Image = [[Image:Puerco en naranja recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Orangy pork</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.8</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Great to cut through the fat of pork</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nAnother [[Mexican]] slow [[Roast pork|roast pork]] recipe that is quite similar to [[Cochinita pibil]]\n[[Image:Puerco en naranja marinading.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Puerco en naranja, marinading]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.5 kg [[Pork shoulder|pork shoulder]]\n| 6 [[Fat|fat]] [[Garlic cloves, peeled and crushed|garlic cloves, peeled and crushed]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] to taste\n| 2 teaspoons [[Mexican oregano]]\n| 12 [[Peppercorns|peppercorns]], crushed\n| 3 large [[Oranges|oranges]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Brown sugar]] or to taste\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Remove and discard rind and large amounts of excess [[Fat|fat]]\n* Stab the [[Meat|meat]] all over with a small sharp knife or cut a shallow cross-hatch pattern in the flesh\n* Make a paste with the [[Juice|juice]] of 1 [[Orange|orange]] together with the [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Peppercorns|peppercorns]], [[Oregano|oregano]] and [[Salt|salt]], reserving the orange skin\n* Rub this mixture all over the [[Pork|pork]] and leave to [[Marinade|marinade]] overnight in a cool place\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the [[Pork|pork]] into a [[Casserole|casserole]] or [[Dutch oven]]\n| Squeeze the [[Juice|juice]] of the second [[Orange|orange]] over the [[Meat|meat]] and cover with the skins of the two [[Oranges|oranges]] and a layer of [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]]. cover with a lid and [[Roast|roast]] for 2 hours\n| Drain all of the juices and reserve, discard the orange skins.\n| Turn the [[Meat|meat]] over, add back 3 tablespoons of the juices and [[Roast|roast]] uncovered for 30 minutes, [[Basting|basting]] now and then. Add more of the reserved juices if it's drying out.\n| Now drain all of the juices and reserve.\n| Roast for a further 30 minutes, turning once.\n| Remove the joint from the [[roasting tray]], cover and rest while you complete the sauce.\n| Skim the reserved [[Juice|juice]]s of any [[Fat|fat]].\n| Add all of the juices and the brown sugar to the [[roasting tray]]\n| Heat and reduce, stirring all the time.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nSlice the [[Meat|meat]], pour the [[Sauce|sauce]] over the [[Meat|meat]] and serve at room temperature.  [[Fried]] [[Onions|onions]], [[Potatoes|potatoes]] and a good [[Chili sauce|chili sauce]] go well with this.\n===Variations===\nAdd a few teaspoons of [[Recado de achiote|recado de achiote powder]] for colour and extra flavour.\n===Chef's note===\nIf you are using a smaller joint, I would still use the same quantity of marinade ingredients.\n===Left overs===\nRefrigerate any leftovers in a [[Lock & Lock box ]]. The meat makes wonderful sandwiches!\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n==See also==\n* Many of our other [[slow roast recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#puercoennaranja #juice #fat #roast #oranges #roastingtray #orange #pork #peppercorns #brownsugar #dutchoven </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This one, unlike the original slow cooked [[Pork shoulder|pork shoulder]] has a whole manner of different flavourings.\n\nWe both chose three of each for ourselves, marked them with [[Cocktail sticks|cocktail sticks]] so we knew which ones were ours.\n\nThe results were fabulous.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 400g unflavoured [[Pulled pork|pulled pork]], already cooked\n| 5 [[Spring onions|spring onions]], finely chopped\n| Half a [[Sweet red pepper|sweet red pepper]], finely chopped\n| 60g [[Cheddar cheese|cheddar cheese]]\n| 6 small white [[Flour tortillas|flour tortillas]]\n}}\n====flavours====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 tablespoon [[Branston pickle|branston pickle]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Curry powder|curry powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Taste Sensation Jalapeno and Lime Seasoning]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Taste Sensation Mexican seasoning]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Taste Sensation fajita seasoning]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Taste Sensation Tangy Chipotle Marinade]]\n| A quick [[Spray|spray]] of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat your [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Pulled pork tortillasBaked.jpg|Baked to perfection - crispy, yet moist inside.\nImage:Pulled pork tortillasReadyToBake.jpg|Rolled and ready to bake\nImage:Pulled pork enchiladas INGREDIENTS.jpg|The ingredients\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Mix the [[Chopped spring onions|chopped spring onions]] and [[Red peppers|red peppers]] together in a large bowl.\n| Divide the mixture into 6 and mix one of your chosen seasonings (or [[Pickles|pickles]]!) into each portion.\n| Fill each [[Flour tortilla|flour tortilla]] with the mixture, roll up and close with a [[Cocktail stick|cocktail stick]] if needed.\n| [[Spray]] a [[Baking tray|baking tray]] with [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and place the rolled [[Enchiladas|enchiladas]] in the tray.\n| Sprinkle with the [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheddar cheese|cheddar cheese]].\n| [[Bake]] for 30 minutes at 180\u00b0 C.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Sour cream|sour cream]], chopped [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and a little torn [[Basil|basil]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilean recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Peruvian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:12032020'>#pulledporkenchiladas #cheddarcheese #pulledpork #oliveoil #spray #sweetredpepper #recipes #branstonpickle #enchiladas #grated #sourcream</code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

They are ideal for freezing\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1875\n|PortionCalories = 468\n|DatePublished=17th March 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 14 hours\n|PrepTime = 12 hours\n|CookTime = 2 hours\n|Image = [[Image:Refried beans.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Better than El Paso</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Fresher and not at all cloying or gloopy (which the tinned stuff is!)</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\n[[Refried beans]] are the essential ingredient for [[:Category:Mexican recipes|Mexican]] and [[:Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Tex-Mex]] dishes.  They are ideal for [[freezing]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 500g (1lb 2oz) [[dried]] [[pinto beans]]\n| 1.2 [[litres]] (2 [[pints]]) water\n| 1 large [[onion]], chopped\n| 250g (9oz) [[smoked]] streaky [[bacon]], finely chopped\n| 1 small [[fresh red chili]], deseeded and finely chopped\n| 2 tablespoons [[olive oil]]\n| knob of [[butter]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Soak the [[beans]] overnight in plenty of water.  Drain and re-rinse.\n| [[Boil]] the [[beans]] in 1.2 [[litres]] (2 [[pints]]) of water boil until tender. Reserve the cooking water.\n| In a large [[frying]] pan or [[wok]], heat the [[oil]] and [[butter]] and [[fry]] the the [[onion]] until soft.\n| Add the [[bacon]] and [[fry]] it until cooked, but not crispy.\n| [[Mash]] the [[beans]], a [[potato ricer]] or [[Potato masher|masher]] is good for this,  then mix them with the [[fried]] [[bacon]] and [[onion]].\n| Stir in a little of the reserved cooking water so the [[beans]] are the same consistency as [[double cream]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot as a [[side dish]] or as an ingredient in your recipe.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#beans #onion #bacon #butter #litres #fry #refriedbeansrecipe #pints #mash #potatoricer #refriedbeans </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Sangrita recipe",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Sangrita recipe Cocktail, from Cookipedia.Co.Uk\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#tequila #tomato #sangritarecipe #juice #mixer #serranochillies #limejuice #lime #oranges #onion #hotchiles \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Sangrita is a tomato juice based drink that is often used as a cocktail mixer or drunk alongside tequila as a chaser\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 134\n|PortionCalories = 67\n|DatePublished=6th August 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Sangrita\n |Servings = Serves 2\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 3 minutes\n |PrepTime = 3 minutes\n |CookTime = None\n |Image = [[Image:Sangrita.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">I thought this would be foul</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">But it's lovely - odd though.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Sangrita''' is a [[tomato]] juice based drink that is often used as a cocktail mixer or drunk alongside [[tequila]] as a chaser. Not to be confused with \"[[sangria]],\" a fruit and wine concoction, this beverage is a tangy mixture of [[tomato]] and [[orange juices]], usually spiked with [[hot chiles]] and [[lime juice]]. It may sound odd in flavour, but sangrita is considered the perfect accompaniment to good quality [[tequila]], like an aged a\u00f1ejo or a good reposado. The [[tequila]] and sangrita are poured into separate [[shot glasses]] and the two are alternately sipped, not chased. First the [[tequila]], then the chilled sangrita. Slowly, one after the other.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 100 ml [[Tomato juice|tomato juice]]\n| [[Juice]] from two large [[Oranges|oranges]]\n| [[Juice]] from one [[Lime|lime]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Grenadine|grenadine syrup]]\n| 1 small [[Onion|onion]], peeled and very finely chopped\n| 2 [[Serrano chillies|serrano chillies]], finely chopped\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]] to taste\n}}\n'''to garnish'''\n* A few [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Blend all of the ingredients in a cocktail [[Mixer|mixer]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe chilled, garnished with [[Coriander|coriander]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Drink and beverage recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tequila #tomato #sangritarecipe #juice #mixer #serranochillies #limejuice #lime #oranges #onion #hotchiles </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Sincronizada recipe",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Sincronizada recipe Cheese, from Cookipedia.Co.Uk\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#cheese #ham #quesadillas #tortillas #sincronizadarecipe #flourtortillas #tortilla #sandwich #grilled #masa #cheddar \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=In Mexican cuisine, the sincronizada is a tortilla-based sandwich\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2455\n|PortionCalories = 1227\n|DatePublished=21st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 2\n |Difficulty = 1\n |ImageComment = A \"sincronizada\", cut into wedges\n |TotalTime = 25 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Sincronizada recipe recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Cheese tortilla sandwich</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I like mine with extra chillies!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n}}\nIn [[Mexican Cuisine|Mexican cuisine]], the sincronizada is a [[Tortilla|tortilla]]-based [[Sandwich|sandwich]]. They are frequently confused with [[Quesadillas|quesadillas]], due to their resemblance to \"quesadillas\" sold in the United States. (U.S. quesadillas are usually made with [[Flour tortillas|flour tortillas]] rather than molded from [[Masa|masa]] in the [[Mexican]] style).\n\nSincronizadas (so called because the top and bottom [[Tortilla|tortilla]] are \"synchronized\" together) [[Sandwich|sandwich]] ingredients between two [[Tortillas|tortillas]]. The sandwich is then [[Grilled|grilled]].\n\n=== The difference between Sincronizadas & [[quesadillas]] ===\n''This is only a rough guide, there are many, many regional differences.''\n* Sincronizadas usually include [[Ham|ham]]\n* Sincronizadas are usually made with [[Wheat flour|wheat flour]] [[tortillas]]\n* Sincronizadas are usually served flat, cut into segments\n* [[Quesadillas]] are usually made with [[corn tortillas]], though can be made with [[flour tortillas]]\n* As well as [[cheese]], [[Quesadillas]] can often contain, meat, [[refried beans]] and vegetables.\n* [[Quesadillas]] are often rolled before serving.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 soft [[Flour tortillas|flour tortillas]]\n| 1 cup [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheese|cheese]].\n| 70g strong [[Cheddar]]. ''Original recipes suggest [[Oaxaca cheese]] or [[Monterey Jack cheese]]''.\n| 4 slices of thinly sliced [[Ham|ham]] or [[Prosciutto|prosciutto]], cut into strips\n| 2 red [[Hot chillies|hot chillies]], de-seeded and thinly sliced (or to taste)\n|* You can use [[Chilli|chilli]] [[Sauce|sauce]] instead if you prefer\n| A few thinly cut slices of fresh [[Tomato|tomato]]\n| A few rings of thinly sliced [[Onions|onions]]\n| A handful of [[Coriander|coriander]] or [[Parsley leaves|parsley leaves]], chopped finely\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Lay two of the [[Tortillas|tortillas]] side-by-side on a flat surface and sprinkle with half of the [[Cheese|cheese]]\n| Layer the half of [[Ham|ham]] on to the [[Cheese|cheese]]\n| Distribute the remaining ingredients apart from the [[Cheese|cheese]] and [[Ham|ham]]\n| Top with the remaining [[Ham|ham]] and [[Cheese|cheese]]\n| Complete the 'sandwiches' by covering with the [[Tortillas|tortillas]]\n| On a [[Griddle|griddle]] or a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]], cook the sincronizadas, one at-a-time until the [[Tortillas|tortillas]] are lightly [[Browned|browned]] and starting to become crispy, turning once\n| Cut each sincronizada into 6 quadrants\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot with [[Guacamole|guacamole]] and a [[Green salad|green salad]]\n===Variations===\nChange the [[Cheddar cheese]] for a Mexican type of cheese that is called [[Oaxaca cheese|\"quesillo/queso oaxaca\"]] which can be easily torn into thinner strands and melts faster. \n\nI usually put some mayonnaise on the tortillas then the ham,cheese, a bit of fried beans, and cover it with the other tortilla with mayonnaise and another slice of ham. -- [[User:Pepekike]] 04:28, 21 July 2011 \n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n* [[Talk:Sincronizada_recipe|Visitor comments]] relating to this recipe\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cheese #ham #quesadillas #tortillas #sincronizadarecipe #flourtortillas #tortilla #sandwich #grilled #masa #cheddar </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Sous vide Tex-Mex pork tenderloin fillet recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#herbs #onion #spice #porktenderloin #sousvide #porkfillet #porktenderloinfillet #blowtorch #tacoseasoning #sousvidetexmexporktenderloinfillet #blend \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Pork tenderloin cooked sous-vide is glorious. I actually cooked this for another recipe, Cheatin' pork enchiladas as I needed pre cooked tenderloin\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 465\n|PortionCalories = 232\n|DatePublished=1st March 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  9 hours, 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  9 hours\n|Image = [[Image:Sous vide TexMex pork tenderloin fillet recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Sort and spicy</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This is exsquisite. The only downside is that you do need a sous vide cooker.  If you've got one, then start cooking!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Pork tenderloin]] cooked [[Sous-vide|sous-vide]] is glorious.  Tender and juicy with a hint of [[Spice|spice]] and [[Herbs|herbs]].  I actually cooked this for another recipe, [[Cheatin' pork enchiladas]] as I needed pre cooked [[Tenderloin|tenderloin]].  This would be fabulous cooked as it is but if you are going to use it in another recipe, try to avoid overcooking the pork in the second recipe or you will lose the benefit of cooking [[Sous vide|sous vide]].\n[[Image:Sous vide TexMex pork tenderloin fillet vac sealed.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Vacuum sealed, ready to cook for 9 hours]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 [[Pork tenderloin fillet|pork tenderloin fillet]] (about 700g)\n| 2 bunches of [[Sage leaves|sage leaves]]\n| &#189; small [[Onion|onion]], peeled and sliced\n| 1 stick of celery, cut into moons\n| 1 tablespoon of [[Old India Taco Seasoning]] or a similar [[Spice|spice]] [[Blend|blend]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| If you have a [[Swiss steak|meat tenderiser]] with metal blades, stamp the tenderloin all over, on both sides.\n| Cut the [[Pork fillet|pork fillet]] into 2 pieces so it will fit into a large vacuum bag together with the [[Onion|onion]] a [[Herbs|herbs]].\n| Seal the bag at one end and add the [[Pork tenderloin|pork tenderloin]], [[Onion|onion]], [[Herbs|herbs]] and [[Spices|spices]].\n| Hold the bag closed and shake well to mix.\n| Wipe the edge to be sealed with a [[Paper towel|paper towel]] to ensure it seals properly.\n| [[Vacuum seal]] the bag.  I like to seal twice at both ends, but that's just the pessimist in me!\n| Cook [[Sous vide|sous vide]] at 59\u00b0C (''138.2\u00b0F'') for up to 9 hours or at least a minimum of 3 hours.\n| Once cooked, discard the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Herbs|herbs]] and any juices.\n| If you want to [[Brown|brown]] the outside, cook in a hot pan with a little [[Butter|butter]] for a few minutes, adding an extra blast of a [[Blowtorch|blowtorch]] if you have one.\n| Slice and serve!\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you are using [[Old India Taco Seasoning]], don't add any [[Salt|salt]] or [[Pepper|pepper]] as this mix is pretty salts already.  However, without Old [[India]] [[Taco seasoning|taco seasoning]], this would be delicious with just a grind of pepper and a pinch of salt added before sealing the bag.\n{{SousVideSeeAlso}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Sous vide recipes]]\n[[Category:Sous vide cooking]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#herbs #onion #spice #porktenderloin #sousvide #porkfillet #porktenderloinfillet #blowtorch #tacoseasoning #sousvidetexmexporktenderloinfillet #blend </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }

Replace the lid and shake like mad to coat the sweet potatoes evenly\n| Peel and quarter the [[Red onions|red onions]] and add the the [[Lock and Lock box]].  Shake more gently this time so as not to separate the [[Onions|onions]] too much\n| Shake the mixture on to the hot [[Baking tray|baking tray]] and [[Bake|bake]] for 40 minutes\n| After 35 minutes, [[Crumble|crumble]] the [[Feta cheese|feta cheese]] over the [[Sweet potatoes|sweet potatoes]] and return to the [[Oven|oven]] for the final 5 minutes\n| Serve hot!\n}}\n===Variations===\n*Try this recipe with a variety of [[chilli sauces]]!\n*Add a [[Tomato salsa|tomato salsa]] to make a tasty [[Vegetarian|vegetarian]] [[Taco|taco]] filling.\n*Swap the [[Sweet potato|sweet potato]] for [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]].  The [[Cooking times|cooking times]] will be similar.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes]]\n[[Category:Squash recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#sweetpotatobake #sweetpotato #redonions #bakingtray #sweetpotatoes #fetacheese #miseenplace #wahaca #tomatosalsa #crumble #driedthyme </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Tex-Mex breaded smoked salmon",
                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Tex-Mex breaded smoked salmon recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#masaharina #salmon #egg #plainflour #breadcrumbs #smokedsalmon #tacoseasoning #breadcrumb #oliveoil #salads #spices \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=We had a packet of thinly sliced smoked salmon leftover from Christmas so I thought rather than eating it raw, I would find a different way to serve it\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 605\n|PortionCalories = 302\n|DatePublished=5th January 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime =  5 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:TexMex breaded smoked salmon recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Again, again? \ud83e\udd17</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">So I ask, what's not to like?</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nWe had a packet of thinly sliced [[Smoked|smoked]]  [[Salmon|salmon]] leftover from Christmas so I thought rather than eating it raw, I would find a way to cook it for a change.\n[[Image:TexMex breaded smoked salmon prep.jpg|thumb|300px|right|The breading production line!]]\n\nI used [[Old India Taco Seasoning]] for the [[Spices|spices]] and [[Masa Harina|masa harina]] where I would normally use [[Plain flour|plain flour]].  If you don't have the Old [[India]] [[Taco seasoning|taco seasoning]] you could use homemade [[Tex-Mex seasoning]], a different [[Taco|taco]] seasoning or your own [[Blend|blend]] of spices.  This was so good, we're having again tonight!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 125g packet of thinly sliced [[Smoked salmon|smoked salmon]]\n| 1 beaten [[Egg|egg]]\n| 5 tablespoons [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Old India Taco Seasoning]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Masa Harina|masa harina]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Separate the [[Smoked salmon|smoked salmon]] sheets and cut them smaller if they are very large.\n| Add the [[Old India Taco Seasoning]] to the [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]] and mix well.  Tip this mix onto a large plate.\n| Add the [[Masa Harina|masa harina]] to one plate and the beaten [[Egg|egg]] to another.\n| Put 3 tablespoons of [[Olive oil|olive oil]] into a large pan and heat gently.\n| Dredge each [[Salmon|salmon]] sheet in [[Masa Harina|masa harina]] (or [[Plain flour|plain flour]]), [[Dip|dip]] it in the beaten [[Egg|egg]] to coat both sides then dredge it through the [[Breadcrumb|breadcrumb]] mix, patting it down to ensure a good covering.\n| Pop the coated [[Salmon|salmon]] into the pan and cook for 2 minutes a side, turning once.  You may need to do this in batches rather than crowding the pan.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a selection of [[Salads|salads]].\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you are using [[Old India Taco Seasoning]], don't add any extra salt as the mix is already quite salty.  If you add extra seasoning, it won't get any spicier, it will just get saltier.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Freshwater fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#masaharina #salmon #egg #plainflour #breadcrumbs #smokedsalmon #tacoseasoning #breadcrumb #oliveoil #salads #spices </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Lupita is a true reflection of the incredible flavours, colours and aromas found throughout Mexico City.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 500 g cooked [[Shredded|shredded]] [[Beef|beef]] brisket\n| 700 g [[Plum tomatoes|plum tomatoes]]\n| 200 g of La Coste\u00f1a green tomatillo\n| 150 g of La Coste\u00f1a Chile Chipotle in Adobo\n| 1 Large [[Onion]], peeled and sliced         \n| 1 whole [[Onion|onion]] peeled and cut in half\n| 45 ml of [[Corn oil|corn oil]]\n| 1 [[Garlic clove|garlic clove]], [[Minced|minced]]\n| 1 sprig of [[Marjoram|marjoram]]\n| 1 sprig of [[Thyme|thyme]]\n| 1 teaspoon of dry [[Mexican oregano|mexican oregano]]\n| \u00bd teaspoon of [[Cracked black pepper]]\n| \u00bd table spoon of [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n}}\n====to serve====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n|16 small Corn Tostadas\n|Tender mix leaf salad\n|200 ml Cr\u00e8me Fraiche\n|100 g of Mexican crumble Queso Fresco\n|1 Avocado hass on slices\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| [[Roast]] the [[Plum tomatoes|plum tomatoes]] and 1 [[Onion|onion]] in half on a flat non-stick pan until everything is soft and the skin is blackened.\n| Place in a mortar or a [[Blender|blender]] and add La Coste\u00f1a Green Tomatillo and [[Chipotle in Adobo]].\n| [[Blend]] perfectly with the pestle or the [[Blender|blender]] until you obtain a thick [[Sauce|sauce]] and reserve.\n| Separately heat the [[Corn|corn]] in a [[Skillet|skillet]] and saut\u00e9 the [[Onion|onion]] slices stirring constantly until you get a golden colour. Add the [[Minced|minced]] [[Garlic|garlic]] and gently saut\u00e9 all together with the [[Marjoram|marjoram]], [[Thyme|thyme]] and [[Mexican oregano]].\n| Pour the mixture of [[Roasted tomatoes|roasted tomatoes]], La Coste\u00f1a Chipotle and [[tomatillos]] and medium [[Fry|fry]] for 10-15 minutes.\n| Season with [[Cracked black pepper|cracked black pepper]] and add half of the [[Salt|salt]]. Stir and check the flavour.\n| Place the [[tostadas]] on a plate and top with the beef Tinga stew.\n| Add [[Cr\u00e8me Fraiche]] to decorate. \n| Sprinkle with crumbled Mexican [[Queso Fresco]]\n| Garnish with the tender mixed salad leaves and a few [[avocado]] slices.\n}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:MexTrade.co.uk recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n===Recipe source===\n{{Template:RecipeCourtesyOfMexTrade.co.uk}}\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#onion #tostadas #crackedblackpepper #mexicanoregano #tingaderes #plumtomatoes #thyme #blender #beef #marjoram #garlicclove </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Edible tortilla baskets recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#tortilla #tortillabaskets #spray #flourtortilla #wheat #brush #oliveoil #flour #yellowcornmeal #taco #miseenplace \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=These edible tortilla pots or baskets are easy to make and create fantastic edible bowls which enhances the appearance (and taste) of any meal\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 237\n|PortionCalories = 29\n|DatePublished=16th December 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Servings: 8 - 1 pack of soft tortillas makes 8 edible bowls\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  31 minutes\n|PrepTime =  25 minutes\n|CookTime =  6 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Tortilla baskets recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Genius!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Such a neat idea.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n}}\n\nThese [[Tortilla pots|tortilla pots]], [[Tortilla|tortilla]] baskets are easy to prepare and make fantastic edible bowls which enhances the appearance (and taste) of any meal.\n\nThis cooking process works just as well with soft [[Flour|flour]] [[Wheat|wheat]] [[Flour tortilla|flour tortilla]] wraps as it does with soft [[Yellow cornmeal|yellow cornmeal]] [[Tortilla|tortilla]] wraps.\n\nThe idea is really simple, [[Spray|spray]] or [[Brush|brush]] the [[Tortilla|tortilla]], shape it into a greased bowl and back it in the [[Oven|oven]].  This hardens it  an turns it into a large crispy edible [[Taco|taco]]!\n\nYou must use an [[Oven|oven]]-proof bowl and you may have to experiment to find the bowl that produces the best shape.  I've found that  a small and a medium [[Glass|glass]] pyrex bowl work really well.\n\nFill them with the food of your choice, you'll find them to be much stronger than you might imagine.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 pack of soft [[Wheat|wheat]] [[Flour tortilla|flour tortilla]] wraps or soft [[Cornmeal|cornmeal]] [[Tortilla|tortilla]] wraps.\n| [[Olive oil]] for spraying for [[Brushing|brushing]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6), [fan oven 180\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Lightly [[Spray|spray]] or [[Brush|brush]] your [[Oven|oven]]-proof bowls so the [[Tortilla|tortilla]] wrap doesn't stick once it has been [[Baked|baked]].\n| Lightly [[Spray|spray]] the top surface of the [[Tortilla|tortilla]] with a little [[Olive oil|olive oil]], not too much.\n| Push the [[Tortilla|tortilla]] into your bowl so it makes a 'useful' shape.\n| [[Bake]] the [[Tortillas|tortillas]], in the bowls for 6 minutes or until they start to colour.\n| Watch them closely as the time between [[Browning|browning]] and burning is really short!\n| Carefully remove the bowls from the [[Oven|oven]] and invert them over [[Paper towels|paper towels]] and knock the shaped [[Tortilla|tortilla]] out onto the paper towels.\n| They remain soft and pliable while they are still hot so leave them upside down for 15 minutes or so to cool and harden, ready for use.\n| If like me, you don't have enough bowls, you can make these in batches, they keep pretty well for a day or so.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\n[[Image:Edible tortilla bowl.jpg.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Lightly greased and ready to bake]]\n</gallery>\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tortilla #tortillabaskets #spray #flourtortilla #wheat #brush #oliveoil #flour #yellowcornmeal #taco #miseenplace </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

title": "Tray-baked butternut squash pisto",
                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Tray-baked butternut squash pisto recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#butternutsquash #traybakedbutternutsquashpisto #oliveoil #pinenuts #bananashallots #ratatouille #toasted #port #cuminseeds #clovesofgarlic #sherryvinegar \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Pisto is the Spanish equivalent of ratatouille. This tray-baked squash pisto is almost a sweet and sour dish, tempered with the sherry vinegar\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1051\n|PortionCalories = 262\n|DatePublished=11th January 2015\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour, 40 minutes\n|PrepTime =  20 minutes\n|CookTime =  1 hour, 15 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Tray-baked butternut squash pisto.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">I-Spy ciabatta!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Superb recipe, thanks Julia.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis recipe was going to be cooked in a pan only but in the end it made far more sense to tray-bake it.  The sugary squash and port, combined with the sherry vinegar make this a sweet and sour dish.\n[[Image:Tray-baked butternut squash pisto oven ready.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Ready for the oven]]\n\n''Pisto is the [[Spanish]] equivalent of [[Ratatouille|ratatouille]].''\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1.2 kg [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]], peeled and chopped into 2cm pieces - about 800g once prepared\n| 1 teaspoon of [[Old India Taco Seasoning]]\n| 6 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| A good pinch of [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 5 [[banana shallots]], peeled and roughly sliced\n| 3 [[Sweet peppers]] of any colour, deseeded, halved and cut into rings\n| 1 [[Indian green chillies|Green Indian chili]], thinly sliced, deseeded if you wish\n| 1 large [[Sprig of rosemary|sprig of rosemary]], left whole\n| 4 freshly picked [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n| 5 [[Cloves of garlic|cloves of garlic]], peeled and smashed\n| 1 teaspoon dried [[Mexican oregano]]\n| 1/2 a teaspoon of dried [[epazote]]\n| 1 teaspoon of whole [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]]\n| A pinch of freshly [[Grated|grated]] [[Nutmeg|nutmeg]]\n| 5cm [2\"] [[cinnamon]] bark\n| A handful of [[green beans]] or other vegetables of choice\n| 180ml [[Passata|passata]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Port|port]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sherry vinegar|sherry vinegar]]\n}}\n''' to garnish'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 tablespoons [[Pine nuts|pine nuts]]\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat your [[oven]] to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6), [fan oven 180\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Pop the [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]] chunks into a [[Lock and Lock box]], add the [[Old India Taco Seasoning]], shake like mad to mix and set to one side.\n| Add the [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]] and all of the [[olive oil]] to a large [[Frying pan]] \n| Gently saut\u00e9 the [[Shallots]] for 15 minutes, adding the whole smashed garlic for the last 5 minutes\n| Pour the Shallots, garlic and oil into a large [[oven tray]]\n| As we're going to add the vegetables next, it's handy to toss them in the pan or wok to soak up all the remaining olive oil.\n| [[Sieve|Sieve]] the [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]] pieces (or pop them into a salad spinner) to remove any liquid that may have leached out.\n| Add the sweet peppers, and all of the herbs and spices to the oven tray and mix really well\n| Cover this with a layer of [[tin-foil]] and bake in the oven for 1 hour\n| After one hour, remove the foil, add the passata, port, sherry vinegar and green beans, mix well and bake, uncovered for 15 minutes.\n| Remove the bay leaves, rosemary sprig and cinnamon and serve.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe garnished with [[Toasted|toasted]] [[Pine nuts|pine nuts]]\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you don't have [[Old India Taco Seasoning]], a pinch of [[Salt|salt]] and &#189; teaspoon of unsmoked [[Paprika]] will work just as well.\n{{Template:Pisto recipes}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Squash recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#butternutsquash #traybakedbutternutsquashpisto #oliveoil #pinenuts #bananashallots #ratatouille #toasted #port #cuminseeds #clovesofgarlic #sherryvinegar </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Wahaca - Mexican Market Eating - Uk Restaurant chain - Cookipedia review\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#wahacamexicanmarketeatingukrestaurantchain #tacos #suppliers #wahacachillisauces #hotsauces #latinamericanrecipes #blackbeans #blackbean #taquitos #quesadilla \n|hashtagrev=12032020\n|description=My review of the fantastic Wahaca, Mexican Market Eating chain after a recent visit to the Covent Garden Restaurant\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n__NOTOC__\n==Wahaca - Mexican Market Eating - UK Restaurant chain==\nI love Mexican food and I think this is the best British Mexican restaurant chain I've been to in a very long while.  If the name already rings a bell, it's probably because you've seen Wahaca's co-founder, Cheltenham born Thomasina Miers on Channel 5's ''Mexican Food Made Simple'' tv cookery program or maybe you remember her as BBC 2's 2005 ''Masterchef'' winner.\n\nWe popped in for a light early evening meal and were instantly impressed.  It has the ''cool'' buzz that I remember from Bob Payton's ''Chicago Pizza Pie Factory'' way back in the 80's.  When we left it even had the matching hoards of people queuing down the stairs to get a table.\n\nFor under \u00a320 we had the Wahaca Street Food Selection for 2 people: 3 pork pibil [[tacos]], 3 winter vegetable [[tacos]], 1 large huitlacoche [[quesadilla]], 2 [[black bean]] tostadas and 2 chicken [[taquitos]] with green rice & [[black beans]].  My favourite way to eat, lots of little portions of different flavoured dishes, which you can eat with your fingers. Unlike some British Mexican restaurant offerings that appear to come straight from the microwave or the deep fat frier, these were cooked to order and packed with fresh vegetables.  Oh and don't forget the mandatory selection of [[hot sauces]] on your table. \n<gallery widths=250px perrow=5>\nImage:Wahaca Covent garden 4.jpg|Facia - Wahaca, 66 Chandos St, Covent Garden, London WC2N 4HG\nImage:Wahaca Covent garden 3.jpg|Lobby / Reception area Wahaca Covent Garden\nImage:Wahaca Mexican Mobile Eating.jpg|The Wahaca Mexican Mobile Eating van, under the trees, Canada Square Park\nImage:Wahaca Covent garden 1.jpg|So light and airy, you would never know you were in the a basement\nImage:Wahaca book of matches - Serrano chilli seeds.jpg|Not a book of matches, the complimentary packet of Serrano chilli seeds we were given as we left!\nImage:Wahaca The South Bank Experiment.jpg|The South Bank Experiment<br />Built from 8 recycled shipping containers!\n</gallery>\nThe decor was cleverly done, it was only as we left, I remembered we had actually been in a windowless basement.  The service was impeccable and everyone was was extremely helpful.  A very slick operation that has been replicated in 11 locations in the South East, 13 if you count the 2 Mexican Mobile Eating vans. Congratulations Tommi, I'm already planning another excuse to get back into London for another Mexican feast!\n\n''Update:'' In the short time since this article was written, we've been to even more Wahaca locations, every time the food and service has been exemplary.  Our last visit, to the South bank Experiment, deserves a special mention.  The restaurant overlooks the river, being situated on a the first floor terrace of the 1950's minimalist building, The Queen Elizabeth Hall, which sits between The Royal Festival Hall and The Hayward Gallery. The 'South Bank Experiment' is so named because of the restaurants unique construction materials. 8 recycled shipping containers!  Now that's what I call recycling.  It also affords wonderful views of the river and should you want to eat on the move, the mobile eating truck is at river level in front of the restaurant.\n\n===Geographic Locations===\n: '''Wahaca title": "Wahaca frijoles",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Wahaca frijoles Mexican recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chorizo #beans #wahacafrijoles #blackbeans #sourcream #onion #coriander #butter #lancashirecheese #garlic #tortilla \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Wahaca serve two versions of friioles negros (black beans) at their restaurants. \"Tommi\" Miers published this recipe when asked by a blogger\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 731\n|PortionCalories = 182\n|DatePublished=27th August 2014\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  20 minutes\n|PrepTime =  5 minutes\n|CookTime =  15 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Wahaca frijoles recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Tex Mex tasty</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Nice and easy way to get your Mexican fix!  Best with Queso Fresco cheese</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Wahaca]] serve two versions of frijoles negros (''[[Black beans|black beans]]'') at their restaurants.  When a blogger asked Thomasina ''\"Tommi\"'' Miers if she could have the recipe, this is what Tommi kindly published.\n\nThe base recipe is the same, the toppings are the variation: crumbled [[Chorizo|chorizo]] or [[Lancashire cheese]] and [[Sour cream|sour cream]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 400g cooked [[Black beans|black beans]]\n| \u00bd [[Red chilli|red chilli]]\n| 2 stems of [[Coriander|coriander]]\n| 50g [[Butter|butter]]\n| 1 small white [[Onion|onion]], finely chopped\n| 2 [[Cloves of garlic|cloves of garlic]], finely chopped\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Cook the [[Onion|onion]] in the [[Butter|butter]] until soft then add the [[Garlic|garlic]] and cook for a further minute. \n| Drain the [[Beans|beans]] reserving the cooking liquid.\n| Add the cooked [[Beans|beans]] with a little of their cooking liquid and whiz in the [[Food processor|food processor]].\n| Remove to a bowl and season to taste.\n| Allow to cool and serve with finely chopped [[Shallots|shallots]], a garnish of [[Coriander|coriander]] and a crumbling of [[Chorizo|chorizo]]. \n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nCrumbled [[Chorizo|chorizo]] ''or'' [[Grated|grated]] [[Lancashire]] and [[Sour cream|sour cream]], a bowl of [[Tortilla|tortilla]] crisps and a cold [[Beer|beer]]!\n===Recipe source===\n\n* http://www.wahaca.co.uk/2009/08/frijoles-recipe/\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Spanish recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chorizo #beans #wahacafrijoles #blackbeans #sourcream #onion #coriander #butter #lancashirecheese #garlic #tortilla </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Wheat flour tortilla, a vegetarian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#tortillapress #shortening #dough #griddle #fat #wheatflourtortillarecipe #masaharina #vegetableshortening #lard #hand #grilled \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=The are cheap to buy, but not expensive and much nicer when homemade. We also have a good recipe for corn tortillas that uses masa harina for that\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3813\n|PortionCalories = 635\n|DatePublished=12th April 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6 \n |Difficulty = 3\n |TotalTime = 45 minutes\n |PrepTime = 30 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Wheat flour tortillas.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Fun to make</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Not too difficult either</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> - [[User:PSmith]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nThe are cheap to buy, but not expensive and much nicer when homemade.\n\nWe also have a good recipe for [[Corn tortillas|corn tortillas]] that uses [[Masa harina|masa harina]] for that real authentic taste.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 800 g [[Plain flour|plain flour]], sifted.\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]].\n| 100 ml [[Hand|hand]]-hot water\n| 100 g [[Vegetable shortening]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Rub the [[Flour|flour]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Shortening|shortening]] together unti it resembles fine [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]].\n| Little by little add the water and mix to a [[Dough|dough]].\n| Cover with a damp cloth and leave for 20 minutes.\n| Divide into golf-ball sized balls or slightly larger.\n| Roll out on a floured worktop.\n| Cook for about a minute on a hot [[Tava|tava]] or [[Griddle|griddle]] pan until they puff up.\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\n[[Vegetable]] [[Shortening|shortening]] is a solid vegetable [[Fat|fat]] such as Crisco or Trex.  [[Lard]] could be used without any problems but the recipe would no longer be vegetarian.\n===Chef's note===\nIf you don't have a [[tortilla press]], use 2 chopping boards or just two sheets of wood as a substitute.  Place ball of [[dough]] between two non-stick surfaces such as small squares of [[Bake-O-Glide]] and stand on them!\n===Suppliers===\nSee the [[Tortilla Press]] page for UK suppliers.\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tortillapress #shortening #dough #griddle #fat #wheatflourtortillarecipe #masaharina #vegetableshortening #lard #hand #grilled </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Yellow rice (Mexican)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Yellow rice (Mexican) Cooking with chillies recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#annattopowder #rice #onion #garlic #chillies #roastedredpeppers #vegetableoil #longgrainrice #chickenstock #achioteseeds #groundachioteseeds \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=An unusual rice dish that uses ground achiote seeds (annatto powder) to colour it\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 796\n|PortionCalories = 132\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 45 minutes \n|PrepTime = 10 minutes\n|CookTime = 35 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Yellow rice (Mexican) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Definitely Mexican</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.3</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Annatto makes this special!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Carla_Cancio-Bello,_J.D.,_on_behalf_of_Cuban_Cuisine_UK|Carla]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Yellow rice (Mexican) ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Yellow rice - The ingredients]]\nAn unusual [[rice]] dish that uses ground [[achiote seeds]] ([[annatto powder]]) to colour it.  Although it's a Mexican dish, it would work in place of any rice dish.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 200g (7 oz) [[long grain rice]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[vegetable oil]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[ground achiote seeds]] ([[annatto powder]])\n| 1 small [[onion]], finely chopped\n| 2 [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves, crushed\n| 475 ml (16 fl oz) good [[vegetable stock|vegetable]] or [[chicken stock]]\n| 50 g (2 oz) pickled [[jalepeno chili slices]]\n| sea [[salt]]\n| Fresh [[coriander leaves]], chopped\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a sieve, rinse the [[rice]] for a few minutes under cold running water  to remove excess starch.  The water should run clear once done\n| Heat the oil in a pan and fry the [[onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] for 4 minutes until soft and translucent\n| Add the [[annatto powder]] and fry for a further 3 minutes\n| Mix the rice into the [[onion]] mix and stir well to coat all of the rice\n| Add the stock, bring to the boil and [[simmer]], covered, for 25 minutes or until the rice has absorbed all of the liquid.  A sheet or so of [[tin-foil]] under the pan lid helps to make a good seal\n| Add extra water if the [[rice]] dries out before it's cooked\n| Add the chopped [[chillies]] and add [[salt]] to taste\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe in a large bowl, garnished with [[coriander]] leaves\n\n===Variations===\n\nServe cold as a salad.\n\nIf you don't want to add [[chillies]], try some sliced [[roasted red peppers]] instead.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Rice]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#annattopowder #rice #onion #garlic #chillies #roastedredpeppers #vegetableoil #longgrainrice #chickenstock #achioteseeds #groundachioteseeds </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

Although it's a Mexican dish, it would work in place of any rice dish.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 200g (7 oz) [[long grain rice]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[vegetable oil]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[ground achiote seeds]] ([[annatto powder]])\n| 1 small [[onion]], finely chopped\n| 2 [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves, crushed\n| 475 ml (16 fl oz) good [[vegetable stock]]\n| 50 g (2 oz) pickled [[jalepeno chili slices]]\n| sea [[salt]]\n| Fresh [[coriander leaves]], chopped\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a sieve, rinse the [[rice]] for a few minutes under cold running water  to remove excess starch.  The water should run clear once done\n| Heat the oil in a pan and fry the [[onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] for 4 minutes until soft and translucent\n| Add the [[annatto powder]] and fry for a further 3 minutes\n| Mix the rice into the [[onion]] mix and stir well to coat all of the rice\n| Add the stock, bring to the boil and [[simmer]], covered, for 25 minutes or until the rice has absorbed all of the liquid.  A sheet or so of [[tin-foil]] under the pan lid helps to make a good seal\n| Add extra water if the [[rice]] dries out before it's cooked\n| Add the chopped [[chillies]] and add [[salt]] to taste\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe in a large bowl, garnished with [[coriander]] leaves\n===Variations===\nServe cold as a salad.\n\nIf you don't want to add [[chillies]], try some sliced [[roasted red peppers]] instead.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments|Rice]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes|Rice]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#onion #annattopowder #rice #chillies #garlic #vegetablestock #simmer #roastedredpeppers #longgrainrice #boiledorsimmered #coriander </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
